CE Documentation Library

CE Documentation Library

The CE Documentation Library lists all available manuals that serve as references on the use of the Customer Enterprise system. The documents are categorized into three groups: Core System Manuals, CE Utility Reference Manuals, and Installation Guides.

Core System Manuals

The CE core system manuals provide information on the setup and configuration of various CE parameters, as well as the implementation of supplementary functionalities supported by the system.

Archiving and Recovery

This manual is a reference to the Archive and Recovery functionality of the CE system. Discussions include the required parameter settings for configuring the relevant functions, as well as examples of how this functionality is used in transaction processes.

Building a Product

This manual is a reference to the process of building a product in CE. It provides step-by-step procedures on how to create a basic CE module, transaction function, and product setting; configure parameters; and attach components to generate a working business product.

Data Objects

This manual serves as a reference for creating and utilizing data objects in the CE system. The discussions provide details on how to build data object templates and data object entities, and how to attach these to the transaction function screen.

Frequently Asked Questions

This document addresses commonly-asked questions on the Customer Enterprise system. Issues on the browser-side (transaction processing), CE Utility, Security Module, and database, among others, are addressed in the discussions.

Interfacing CE with CS Eximbills

This document discusses the process of interfacing CE with the CS Eximbills (CSX) back office system. Employing the MQ, FTP, and TCP/IP communication protocols, the interface process using the XML format is detailed in this document.

Interfacing CE with Eximbills Enterprise

This document discusses the process of interfacing CE with the Eximbills Enterprise (EE) back office system. Employing the MQ protocol, the interface process for the transfer of data between CE and EE using the XML format is detailed in this document.

Log Settings

This manual provides details on CE logs as well as general instructions on log configuration in CE. This is especially written for the users who are in charge of maintaining the CE system.

Look and Feel

This manual is a reference guide on designing the CE user interface (i.e., the look and feel of the system). Divided into two parts, the manual provides instructions on creating a) the basic L&F style of CE; and b) the CE L&F style that incorporates widgets.

Multi-Entity

This manual is a reference on implementing the Multi-Entity functionality of the CE system. Discussions cover the implementation and application of CE multi-entity.

Multi-Language

This manual discusses the procedures required in setting up the Multi-Language functionality of CE as it is run by Administrator- and Operator-type users. Furthermore, the configuration of certain system and browser elements as well as the setup of related system parameters is explained in step-by-step procedures.

Reports

This manual is a comprehensive reference guide on the requirements and processes involved in building business products and functions that generate online reports and documents.

Security and System Maintenance Functions

This manual is a comprehensive guide on the security and system maintenance of the CE system. As such, it includes detailed instructions for company and company function management, and user and user function management. Maintenance of key functionalities such as authorization rules, reference numbers, and other services is covered as well. In addition, this document discusses the security concepts in CE to assist users assigned with access rights to the CE Security Module.

Standing Data Functions

This document discusses the functions for the CE standing data that are maintained by operators (e.g., parties, clauses). It includes sections for each function, starting with a brief description of the function, followed by the function input when necessary, and the procedure steps.

Supplementary Functions

This manual is a reference for the CE Utility operator user in configuring parameter, JSP, and transaction function settings to define special or supplementary CE functionalities such as uploading images, sending images and forms to the back-office system, and sending notifications via e-mail, SMS, and widgets.

System Administration Functions

This manual is a reference for the default Super Administrator user of the CE Utility in the configuration and maintenance of the CE environment. It discusses in detail user management and parameter management.

System Reference

This document serves as a quick reference to the following elements that are used when configuring specific parameters in the CE Utility: global system parameters, system parameters, components, XML Generator items, server side system methods, system JS methods, and APIs.

CE Utility Reference Manuals

The CE Utility Reference set of manuals is a guide on the use of the Customer Enterprise Utility Workbench, or simply CE Utility. This reference provides details on every function or feature in the CE Utility and includes instructions and step-by-step procedures on how to operate or use the function in relation to operating and maintaining the CE system and processing a business transaction.

A manual is provided for each function group of the CE Utility:

  • CE Utility Reference: User Manager Functions, for the functions that belong to the User Manage function group of the CE Utility when accessed by an Administrator or Operator user

  • CE Utility Reference: Parameter Manager Functions, for the functions that belong to the Parameter Manage function group of the CE Utility when accessed by an Administrator or Operator user

  • CE Utility Reference: System Functions, for the functions that belong to the System Function group of the CE Utility.

  • CE Utility Reference: Transaction Functions, for the functions that belong to the Transaction Function group of the CE Utility.

  • CE Utility Reference: Product Functions, for the functions that belong to the Product Function group of the CE Utility.

  • CE Utility Reference: Maintenance Functions, for the functions that belong to the Maintenance function group of the CE Utility.

    Installation Guides

    The CE installation guides are references on the installation and setup processes of the CE system on different application servers and databases.

Installation Guide WAS 9.0 - Oracle 19c

This is a reference for installing the CE system on WebSphere Application Server Version 9.0.5.6, with an Oracle 19c database. This includes detailed instructions on configuring the components that are required to successfully run CE.

Introduction

  • system overview

  • manual overview

System Overview

CE Look and Feel, or CE L&F, pertains to the CE user interface that is designed when the different elements that make up a functional transaction page are put together based on a desired output.

Generally, CE supports two types of L&F: a basic style, and one that supports the Widget functionality.

Manual Overview

Purpose

This manual serves as a guide on designing the CE user interface (i.e., the look and feel of the system). It provides instructions on:

  • Creating the basic look and feel style of CE

  • Creating CE look and feel style that incorporates widgets

    This document is written with the assumption that:

  • The CE environment has already been successfully installed; and

  • The reader has sufficient knowledge on building a CE product and running the CE Utility functions

  • The reader has sufficient knowledge on the following programming languages and software, which are used in designing the L&F of the CE system:

  • HTML

  • CSS

  • JavaScript

  • Cross-browser scripting (CE V3 supports IE 6+ and Firefox versions higher than 2.0)

  • DreamWeaver

Audience

This manual is a reference specifically for, but not limited to, the following users:

  • Consultants responsible for creating the transaction screens and maintaining the system look and feel.

    Prerequisites

  • Suggested titles before reading this manual: CE Building a Product and CE Utility References

NOTE: Some features discussed in this manual have been tested and documented based on an older system version. Unless otherwise specified, the overall functionality is the same when recreated in the current version.

Using the CE Utility

  • Running the CE Utility

  • Generating the XML Parameter Files

  • BUILDING A PRODUCT

Running the CE Utility

The Customer Enterprise Utility Workbench, or CE Utility, is the main tool for building parameters in CE.

Preparing the CE Utility Files

Along with the installation files, the CE Utility folder is provided with every CE system release. Prior to using the CE Utility, do the following:

  1. Copy the CE Utility folder to the local drive.

  2. Define the required environment variables.

  3. Map the CE directories (e.g., CEWeb.war and CE_PARA) to the network drive.

Figure 2. 1 CE Utility Folder

NOTE:

  1. The default drives defined in the GEN_XML_ROOTPATH and GEN_WEB_ROOTPATH system parameters are O:\ and P:\ respectively. These drives, if currently not existing, may be created through a batch file. While O:\ and P:\are the default drives for CE, these may be set to any other preferred drive available in the network.

  2. To enable users to use the CE Utility on their own local machines as clients connecting to the CE server: 1) Install the Java Development Kit (JDK) program; 2) Copy the CE Utility folder; 3) Create the JAVA_HOME environment variable, which must point to this directory: [Java Home]\[Installed JDK].

  3. For more details on setting up the CE environment, refer to the CE installation guides*.*

  4. For details on the CE Utility functions, refer to the CE Utility Reference manuals.

Batch File for Creating the CE Drives The batch file for creating drives contains the following commands: subst O: /d subst P: /d subst O: C:"\Program Files\IBM\WebSphere\AppServer\profiles\AppSrv01\installedApps\DOCS-CEV336Node01Cell\CE.ear\CE_PARA” subst P: C:"\Program Files\IBM\WebSphere\AppServer\profiles\AppSrv01\installedApps\DOCS-CEV336Node01Cell\CE.ear\CEWeb.war”

Accessing the CE Utility

The main program for running the CE Utility is the CEUtility.bat file, which is found in the CE Utility folder.

Do the following . . .
1. Run the CEUtility batch program to access the CE Utility. NOTE: A shortcut for the CEUtility batch file can be created on the desktop for easy access.
2. The logon window of the CE Utility is displayed. To define the database information, click on the Profile button.
3. In the Database Information dialog box that is displayed, specify the required database details and click on the Save button.
4. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the OK button.
NOTE: This new data source setting is saved in the UserInfo.xml file in the CE Utility directory.
5. The relevant username and password may then be specified for logging on the CE Utility. NOTE: For details on defining CE Utility user profiles, refer to the CE System Administration Functions manual.
6. The CE Utility window is displayed.
7. A function is accessed by opening or double-clicking on the relevant function group and clicking on the function name. NOTE: A user may only access and utilize the functions assigned to him. For more details, refer to the CE Utility Reference - User Manager Functions documentation*.*

NOTE: It is sometimes required to assign a new user name and password when the new database is restored from a backup file. Restoring the backup file restores the original user profiles.

The new user profiles for the CE Utility (as well as the CE Security Module) can be defined during the installation process. SQL scripts are run to create these profiles. Refer to the CE installation guides for more details.

Navigating the CE Utility Interface

After logging on, the CE Utility window is displayed and parameters may then be configured. The functions used for setting up parameters may be accessed by clicking on the function name on the Function menu or by using the shortcut buttons.

The CE Utility interface also provides ways by which parameters can be created, edited, deleted or linked to other operations: menu bar, toolbar buttons, and popup menu.

Figure 2. 2 The CE Utility Interface

NOTE: A function is only displayed, and its corresponding button or menu option enabled, if the user has been given the right to access this function. Some options and functions are only available to Super Administrator users, while others are only accessible to Administrator and Operator users.

CE Utility Functions

The functions that may be accessed for setting up parameters are organized together into several function groups. The current available function groups and their corresponding functions in the CE Utility are as follows:

User Manager Function Group

This function group is comprised of functions used for creating, configuring, and exporting Bank-Country group settings; creating new users; and configuring data sources. These functions are:

  • Business Unit Config

  • DataSource Manage

  • Import/Export Business Unit

  • User Manage

Parameter Manage Function Group

This function group consists of functions used for maintaining system-wide parameters and components. These functions are:

  • AP Server

  • Component Manage

  • Language Configuration

  • System Parameter

  • System Parameters

System Function Group

This function group consists of functions used for maintaining and facilitating system-wide tasks, operations, and settings. These functions are:

  • Image Type Maintain

  • Output Device

  • Queue Manager

  • STP Setting

  • Time Zone

Transaction Function Group

This function group is comprised of functions used for defining the actual business parameters of transaction functions. These facilitate the maintenance and processes of the business transaction modules. These functions are:

  • Amount/Rate Format

  • Batch Manage

  • Clause

  • DO Get Data

  • Export Setting

  • Form

  • GAPIs Setting

  • Get Data

  • Image Control

  • Message Broker Setting

  • Module & Event

  • Report Template

  • STPs Mapping

  • Sub Tasks

  • SWIFT Config

  • System Maintain

  • Transaction Function

  • Transfer To

  • TSU Mapping

  • Upload Message Setting

  • Web Service Setting

  • Widget Maintain

Product Function Group

This function group consists of functions that are used for creating and configuring the products to be accessed and used by the customers or end-users. These functions are:

  • Fields Select

  • Inbox

  • Product Authorize

  • Product Authorize Setting

  • Product Catalog

  • Product Function Setting

  • Product Item

Maintenance Function Group

This function group is comprised of functions used for facilitating the maintenance of data from CE tables, including fields and error settings. These functions are:

  • DB Dictionary

  • Error Handling

  • Error Message Config (CE)

  • Field Conversion

  • Multi Language

  • Page Dictionary

  • XML Generator

    Menu Bar

    The options on the menu bar are shortcuts to both the common and specific functions and tasks of the system.

Figure 2. 3 Menu Bar

Menu Description
File The available options in the File menu are: New: This is used for creating a new parameter or rule. Save: This is used for saving the created or modified settings. Close Function: This is used for closing the current function window. Connect To: This is used for connecting to another Meta data source. Log Off: This is used for logging off a user that is logged on to the system without exiting the system. Exit: This is used for closing the system window and exiting the system.
Edit The available options in the Edit menu are: Add: This is used for adding a setting for the selected function or parameter. Delete: This is used for deleting or removing an existing setting. Edit: This is used for editing or modifying existing settings. Copy: This is used for copying or duplicating a selected setting. Find: This is used for finding a specific setting.
Function The available options in the Function menu are: User Manage, which displays options for running User Manager functions Parameter Manage, which displays options for running Parameter Manager functions System Function, which displays options for running System functions Transaction Function, which displays options for running Transaction functions Product Function, which displays options for running Product functions Maintenance, which displays options for running Maintenance functions
Tools The available options in the Tools menu are: Toolbar: When this option is marked, the toolbar is displayed on the CE Utility Workbench window. Function Toolbar: When this option is marked, the function toolbar is displayed on the CE Utility Workbench window. Set User Profile DB Info: This option is used by the Super Administrator user to change the user information that is to be used by the CE Utility for connecting to a database. Window Style: Selecting this option displays a list of CE Utility interface styles: Microsoft Style, Unix Style, Java Style, Classic Style, and Metal Style. The preferred style may be marked accordingly.
Help The available options in the Help menu are: Help Topics: This is currently not used. Content Help: This is currently not used. About Customer Enterprise: Selecting this option displays the About Customer Enterprise window, which indicates the version information of CE.

Popup Menu

Inside a function or configuration window, options may be provided in the form of a popup menu. This menu is displayed by right-clicking on the relevant window section or on the relevant details.

Figure 2. 6 Popup Menu

  • New

  • Add

  • Sharable

Generating the XML Parameter Files

The created parameters and business logic are stored in the database as Meta data. For this Meta data to be accessible to the application server (AP) and the web server, it has to be converted to XML – the format used for the communication between the client and the server.

The XML files are generated through the XML Generator function of the Maintenance function group in the CE Utility. In most cases, the XML Generator function must be run when a parameter is created or modified using the functions discussed in this document.

Do the following . . .
1. Log on CE Utility as an Administrator or Operator user with rights to the XML Generator function.
2. The CE Utility window is displayed. Run the XML Generator function from the Maintenance function group. Alternatively, click on the XML Generator button in the function toolbar.
3. The XML Generator function window is displayed. When there are newly defined or modified parameters, the Meta Data to XML window is also displayed. It lists these parameters for easy selection. In this case, the parameter can be selected from this window and the Apply button clicked. Afterwards, proceed to Step 5. Alternatively, the Meta data or parameter can be manually selected from the main XML Generator window. In this case, click on the Close button of the Meta Data to XML window and proceed to Step 4.
4. Double-click on the relevant parameter type from the XML Generator window.
5. Depending on the selected parameter type, an XML configuration window may be displayed. In other cases, the process directly proceeds to Step 6. If the configuration window is displayed, indicate the exact or any additional setting required to generate the relevant XML files. When the specifications are defined click on the Save button
6. A message is displayed confirming if the XML files are to be generated on the system path.
NOTE: The path of the XML files is defined through the GEN_XML_ROOTPATH Utility Workbench system parameter. This system parameter is configured through the System Parameter function from the Parameter Manage function group.
7. To save the XML file on the relevant system path, click on the Yes button. To specify another path, click on the No button. On the Save dialog box that is displayed, browse for the path and click on the Save button.
8. When the relevant XML files are generated, the system displays a confirmation message. NOTE: To hide the information on the paths of the generated XML files, click on the Hide button.
NOTE: Check the indicated path(s) to see the generated XML files.

Building a Product

When building a product in the CE Utility, a few prerequisites are required to be met to make sure that modules or products are built in accordance with the bank’s requirements. One step is the GAP analysis which involves an evaluation of transaction requirements, based on the process flow (e.g., fields, clauses, forms, and interfaces). These are required for identifying the fields required for anticipating the required output. When the analysis has been completed, the project team can now begin the process of building a product for the bank’s customers.

The following are steps in building a product:

  1. Access the CE Utility. To access the CE Utility for building parameters, an Operator user must be created by an Administrator user. This is set up through the User Manager function in the User Manage function group.

  2. Set up the module and events. This involves naming the module and the projected events that manage the transaction flow within the module. This is set up in the Module and Event function in CE Utility.

  3. Set up the transaction tables. This involves creating the tables in the DB Dictionary function in CE Utility. There can be different types of tables but only three are mandatory for a CE module: master, ledger, and event.

    NOTE: It is possible to create tables directly into the database by running SQL scripts in the database. In this case, tables can be created before modules and events. It is recommended, however, to use the DB Dictionary for creating tables.

  4. Add fields to the transaction table. Fields must be added to a transaction table and field properties defined for the processing and storage of data. These can be done through the DB Dictionary function in CE Utility.

  5. Set up the transaction functions. This involves creating the functions that correspond to actual business transaction processes. This is done through Transaction Function in the Transaction Function group.

  6. Set up the transaction parameters. This involves designing the transaction screen, defining attribute and catalog settings, and attaching these parameters to the transaction function. These can be done through Transaction Function in CE Utility.

  7. Create the product. The product is the actual functionality accessed and run by the end-user. This process of creating a product involves setting up the product group, product, and product function, and defining product catalog settings.

  8. Define authorization rules. Authorization rules are set to further define or set limits for authorizing transactions.

  9. Calculation. This involves configuring the transaction JS files and defining calculation functions using available system methods. There are three JS files that have to be configured: the Module Base JS file, Event JS file, and Function JS file.

  10. Define the settings for the transaction input. Certain functions may be added to aid in the input of data into the transaction. The CE Utility provides options for setting up field conversion rules, lookup buttons, customer reference numbers, clauses, dropdown lists, and data objects for this purpose.

  11. Define the settings for the transaction output. Some business transactions involve output generation (i.e., Forms). To make this option available, certain settings must be configured using the functions from the Transaction Function group in CE Utility.

  12. Define the security settings in the CE browser. The products and functions created are assigned to an end-user through the browser-side Security and System Maintenance functions.

    NOTE: The browser-side security and system maintenance functions of CE are often collectively called the Security Module.

  13. Add the Inbox functionality. Another way of accessing a product or a transaction for further processing is through the Customer Inbox. This can be set up through the Inbox function in CE Utility.

NOTE: For more details on configuring different parameters in CE, refer to the CE Utility Reference manuals*.*

Logon Page

End-users access CE by entering their credentials on the logon page.

The button, file name, and JavaScript function for this page are as follows:

Button Name File Name JS Function Name
LOGON SYS_index.htm Login()

Figure 3. 1 Logon Page

Resetting the Password

The CE logon page includes the I Forgot My Password link, which allows the system to send a new password to the user through e-mail. To use this link:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the I Forgot My Password link.
2. The Forgotten Password page is displayed.
Specify the e-mail address to which the password reset link is to be sent. Click on the Continue button.
3. If only one user uses the specified e-mail address, the system proceeds to the next step. If multiple users use the e-mail address: The Login ID field is displayed. Select the relevant login Id.
Click on the Confirm button.
4. A message is displayed confirming that an e-mail is sent to the specified e-mail address. This e-mail contains the link that enables the user to reset the password.

NOTE: The password of the CE user must conform to the following rules:

  1. It must be at least 8-characters long.

  2. It must contain an uppercase character, a lowercase character, and a digit.

  3. It must not contain any special characters.

  4. It must not contain more than three consecutive digits or more than three consecutive identical characters.

  5. It must not contain the user account or name.

  6. It must not be the same as recently used passwords

Inbox

The Inbox shows the statistics or count for transaction statuses. It is also another way to access business transactions. Inbox elements are defined in the CE Utility.

The system generates a JavaScript data array to create the inbox table on the CE page: TOTALARRAY. This data array is included in the SYS_FRAME IFrame.

The default system methods for creating the inbox table are in this file –

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]\SYS_JS\SYS_inbox.js

The default inbox layout is defined in –

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]\SYS_LF_JS\LF_SYS_inbox.js

To customize the inbox, add the related JavaScript methods in this file to control the data array –

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]\JS\Inbox.js

Figure 3. 4 Example of an Inbox

Inbox The inbox contains columns based on the statuses of the transactions (e.g., Saved, Rejected by Supervisor, Awaiting Corporate Approval). The status hyperlink of each column in the inbox may be clicked on in order to access the listed transactions. NOTE: Refer to section Part II: CE Widget Framework for more details on widgets. Example: Log on to the CE system as an operator user. In the CE landing page, the Inbox is displayed. Click on the Saved status hyperlink. The catalog for saved transactions is shown. Select the relevant record and click on the Modify button. The transaction may then be processed in its corresponding function. When accessing the status hyperlink of the inbox, the following error may be encountered: To resolve this error, the following configurations must be applied: Log on to the CE Utility as an operator user. Run the Inbox function in the Product Function group. Under the Item node, click on the Bank Message option. Edit the Custom Criteria type. Modify the criteria in the Criteria Edit tab and add the following condition: C_MODULE NOT IN (‘UPLD’_‘TRAN’) Generate the inbox_set_item.xml file in the Inbox parameter. This file is generated on the following paths: [Parameter Folder]\CSBANK\US\AP\PRODUCT [Parameter Folder]\CSBANK\WEB\AP\PRODUCT Modify the content of the LF_SYS_inbox.js file. This file is stored on the following path: [CEWeb.war Folder]\SYS_LF_JS function clickInboxItem(_cell){ try { var cellIndex = _cell.cellIndex; var allTotal = 0; var parentTable = _cell.parentNode.parentNode; var parentRows = parentTable.childNodes; var rowCounts = parentRows.length; var vTitle = null; var parentRow = null; for (var i = 1; i < rowCounts; i++) { parentRow = parentRows[i]; var itemCellObj = parentRow.cells.item(cellIndex); if (itemCellObj != null) { var everyCellCount = parseInt(itemCellObj.innerHTML); allTotal = allTotal + everyCellCount; if (everyCellCount > 0) { vTitle = itemCellObj.getAttribute(“titleName”); continue; } } } if (allTotal == 0) { var msg = _getClientMessage(90163); _SYS_Display_WARN(msg); return; } var vItemID = _cell.getAttribute(“itemId”); _clickInbox(vItemID, “selItem”, vTitle, vItemID); } catch (E) { SYS_Display_Exception(“LF_SYS_inbox.clickInboxItem”, E); } }
function setNavigation(){ try { var titleNav = document.getElementById(“titleNav”); var itemNav = document.getElementById(“itemNav”); if(typeof(TITLE_NAME)!="undefined”&&typeof(ITEM_ID)!="undefined”){ titleNav.innerHTML = " > " + TITLE_NAME + " “; itemNav.innerHTML = “> " + ITEM_ID; } if(SEL_TYPE=="selItem”){ titleNav.innerHTML = “"; } } catch (E) { SYS_Display_Exception(“LF_SYS_inbox.setNavigation”, E); } }

NOTE: Certain criteria in the Inbox catalog are displayed using field conversion (e.g., Finance Type field). If an error is encountered when loading this field option, the attribute staticModule must be added into the field conversion setting in order to specify the module name for the field.

Example:

Error

Solution

Update the catalog criteria jsp file by adding the staticModule attribute in the field conversion tag.

Main Function Pages

The three types of main function pages are transaction screens, standing data screens, and security screens.

Transaction Screens

Transaction Page

A transaction module contains at least one transaction function that is attached to a product, which can be a product of the bank or an additional banking service. The transaction module is in charge of managing the processing flows of a transaction. Data input for transactions is facilitated through the fields in this page.

The transaction pages that are retrieved during runtime are placed in this path in the Web folder –

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]\[BANK]\[COUNTRY]\WEB\SCRN

This path is specified in the WEB_SRCPATH system parameter.

Figure 3. 5 WEB_SRCPATH System Parameter

The following table outlines the buttons used in a transaction page, the corresponding JavaScript files and methods performed.

Button Name File Name JS Function Name
CANCEL SYS_JS\SYS_Common.js _Cancel_ToPrevious()
TEMPLATE SYS_JS\SYS_DealButton.js TemplateBtn()
SAVE SYS_JS\SYS_BaseFunc_CAL.js _save_onclick()
CONFIRM SYS_JS\SYS_BaseFunc_CAL.js _submit()

Figure 3. 6 Transaction Page

NOTE: Previous and Next buttons are not system standard buttons. The navigation buttons, as well as the tabs and help tips, are part of the L&F to be defined by the bank.

JSP Template

A page template is provided to define the sections that are common to all transaction screens: page header, main menu, and page footer. A JSP file is provided for each of these sections; these JSP files are consolidated and declared in one JSP file that functions as the JSP template for the transaction page.

Figure 3. 7 Transaction Screen Layout

When restructuring the screen layout, only the template has to be modified. More time can be devoted to the design and content of the main transaction screen.

Figure 3. 8 Main Transaction Screen

At runtime, the system locates the template file first, which then dynamically includes and calls the main transaction page.

CE Utility Setting

When setting the Screen attribute of the transaction function, the following files must be included.

JSP File Description
Main JSP File Browse for the main transaction screen.
Template File Browse for the transaction template file: Trx_Template.jsp. The file is placed in this path – [WEB SERVER DRIVE]\Templates

Figure 3. 9 Transaction Screen Function Component

Inquire History

The Inquire History pages pertain to transaction functions that are used for inquiring on the history of a transaction; specifically, the events of a transaction and the authorization history of the transaction. This type of function consists of two types of pages; event list page and event page.

Event List Page

The event list page shows a list of the transaction’s events. (Clicking on an event displays the event page.)

The event list page for Inquire History functions is defined in this file –

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]\screen\SYS_CE_Inquire_TrxDetailList.jsp

The following table outlines the buttons used in an event list page, as well as the corresponding JavaScript files and methods performed.

Button Name File Name JS Function Name
CANCEL N/A self.close()
SELECT screen\SYS_CE_Inqire_TrxDetailList.jsp viewTrx()
View Auth History screen\SYS_CE_Inqire_TrxDetailList.jsp _View_onclick(this)

Figure 3. 19 Event List Page

Event Page

The event page displays the data of a transaction at a particular stage in the processing flow. (It is displayed upon clicking on the event name in the event page list.)

No special screen is required for the actual event (transaction) page as the system retrieves the original transaction screen defined in CE Utility.

The Cancel button is dynamically added to the event page. The button name, file name, and JavaScript performed are as follows:

Button Name File Name JS Function Name
CANCEL N/A window.parent.close()

Figure 3. 20 Event Page

Change User Profile

The Change User Profile pages pertain to the function used for changing the password and e-mail address of the logged-on user. It is accessed through CE User link on the landing page.

This function consists of two types of pages: change user profile page and confirmation page.

NOTE: The user password can also be changed using the I Forgot My Password link provided in the Logon Page. Refer to the Logon Page > Resetting Password section for information on this procedure.

Change User Profile Page

The Change User Profile page consists of two sections: Change Password and Change Email. This page is defined in this file –

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]\screen\SYS_UserProfile.jsp

Each section is provided with a set of Reset and Confirm buttons that are used for resetting and confirming the password and the e-mail address, respectively.

The following table outlines the Change User Profile page buttons and the corresponding methods performed.

Button Name Change Password Change Email
RESET OnInit() initEmailBox()
CONFIRM Confirm() confirmEmail()

NOTE: Clicking on the Change Password – Confirm button only saves the new password even when a new e-mail is specified (in the Change Email section). In order to modify the e-mail address, access the Change User Profile Page again, change the e-mail address, and click on the Change Email – Confirm button.

Figure 3. 26 Change User Profile Page

NOTE: The password of the CE user must conform to the following rules:

  1. It must be at least 8-characters long.

  2. It must contain an uppercase character, a lowercase character, and a digit.

  3. It must not contain any special characters.

  4. It must not contain more than three consecutive digits or more than three consecutive identical characters.

  5. It must not contain the user account or name.

  6. It must not be the same as recently used passwords.

Main Menu

Main Menu

The main menu is the common way by which a function is accessed and run. (Another way is through the inbox.)

The L&F of the main menu varies according to the bank requirements.

Figure 4. 1 Example 1 Figure 4. 2 Example 2

Figure 4. 3 Example 3

Creating the Main Menu

The overall functionality of the main menu is defined in these JS files.

JS File Description
\SYS_JS\ SYS_menu.js This contains the codes for building or designing the main menu.
\SYS_JS\ SYS_menu_event.js This contains the codes running the functions in the main menu.

To change the L&F of the main menu:

  1. Create a standalone JS file for building the main menu as required.

  2. Declare this standalone JS file in the transaction screens. Make sure that the SYS_menu.js file is removed from the codes

  3. Declare the SYS_menu_event.js file in all the transaction screens or in the Common.jsp file:

Generating the Main Menu

The Function Access Permission (FAP) of the CE user, assigned in the Security Module, determines the type of menu to be created for the user. Specifically, a JavaScript data array is generated.

Declare <CETAGS:GetMenuArray/> files located in the following directory:

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]\ Templates

The data array, strArray, contains the following parameters:

Array Index Parameter Description Example
0 Module This refers to the 4-character module name. SECU
1 Product Id This refers to the product Id. P06031300000
2 Product Name This refers to the product name. Authorization User Rule by Function
3 Function Id This refers to the function Id. F05030700553
4 Function name This refers to the function name. Add Auth User Rule by Func
5 Item Id This refers to the item Id. New
6 Item Name This refers to the item name. New
7 Product Type This refers to the product type – ‘S’ (Security) or ‘T’ (Transaction).
8 New/Cata This refers to the type of screen produced when a product is clicked: a new (initiation) screen or a catalog screen. This is now supported in CE V2.1.0.
9 Catalog Number This refers to the number of catalogs in the catalog screen. As this is currently not supported in CE V2.1.0, the value is: 1.
10 Module Description This refers to the description of the module. Security Module
11 Product Description This refers to the description of the product. Operator Class Maintain
12 Function Description This refers to the description of the function. Add Operator Class

The strArray data array generated follows this format:

[“[MODULE]”, “[PRODUCT ID]”, “[PRODUCT NAME]”, “[FUNCTION ID]”, “[FUNCTION NAME]”, “[ITEM ID]”, “[ITEM NAME]”, “[PRODUCT TYPE]”, “[NEW/CATA]”, “[CATALOG NUMBER]”. “[MODULE DESCRIPTION]”, “[PRODUCT DESCRIPTION]”]

EXAMPLE:

[“IMLC”,“P08071500000”,“Import Letters of Credit”,“F05030700829”,“Apply for Import LC”,“New”,“New”,“T”,“new”,“1”,“Import Letters of Credit”,“Import Letters of Credit”,“Apply for Import LC”]

Figure 4. 4 Example of an HTML Source Code

This JavaScript file contains the commands for creating the main menu, and may be modified to produce different menu styles: [WEB SERVER DRIVE]\JS\MainMenu.js. Refer also to Chapter Eight > MainMenu.js discussion for sample content of the MainMenu.js file.

Running a Menu Function

When a user selects a function from the main menu, the onClick() event of the main menu is executed. Depending on the project involved, either of the following functions has to be called in order to execute this event:

  • funcItemClick (modDesc, pdtID, funcID, itemID, modName)

  • _funcItemClick(sSelectedFuncId)

These methods are defined in the following file –

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]\SYS_JS\SYS_menu_event.js

Figure 4. 5 SYS_menu_event.js File

System CSS Classes

System CSS Classes

For system purposes such as field validation and date formatting, system CSS classes are provided. These CSS classes are located in the following directory: [WEB SERVER DIRECTORY]/theme

Each of the fields in the JSP screen, including hidden fields, must be assigned a valid system CSS class, the naming rule of the which is: [DATA TYPE]_[FIELD TYPE].

The following table lists the available system CSS classes.

Class Name Description Example
AMT_M Mandatory amount field LC Amount
AMT_O Optional amount field Finance Amount
AMT_P Protected amount field LC Balance
INT_M Mandatory integer field Tenor Days
INT_O Optional integer field Positive Tolerance
INT_P Protected integer field Amendment No
FLOAT_M Mandatory float field Interest Rate
FLOAT_O Optional float field Interest Rate
FLOAT_P Protected float field Interest Rate
CHAR_M Mandatory character field Beneficiary Name
CHAR_O Optional character field Beneficiary ID
CHAR_P Protected character field Collection Reference No
DATE_M Mandatory date field Expiry Date
DATE_O Optional date field Tenor Start Date
DATE_P Protected date field Issued Date
TIME_M Mandatory time field Transaction Time
TIME_O Optional time field Registration Time
TIME_P Protected time field Login Time

Figure 5. 1 Example of a CSS File

Using Other CSS Files

The system CSS files provided can be modified as required. Aside from these, project-designed CSS files can also be used. These are also saved in the same directory where the system CSS files are located.

FTL Files

FTL Files

Freemarker Template (FTL) files are templates that can be embedded into the JSP file. These are used to generate text and define the look and feel of pages in a transaction screen.

By modifying the related FTL files, the L&F of screens that are generated by CE tags such as GetTranCata can be defined or changed. All FTL files are stored in the following directories:

  • [WEB SERVVER DRIVE]\WEB-INF\FTL

  • [WEB SERVVER DRIVE]\Templates\FTL

The following are the available FTL files that can be modified according to business or functional requirements:

  • BatchManage.ftl

  • CompareEventList.ftl

  • CUBKCRITERIA.ftl

  • CustRef.ftl

  • ErrorContent.ftl

  • GetAuthGroups.ftl

  • GetButtonInfo.ftl

  • GetConfirmData.ftl

  • GetCriteria.ftl

  • GetTranCata.ftl

  • IncomingXml.ftl

  • INQCUBK.ftl

  • NotificationCata.ftl

  • OperatorClass.ftl

  • OperatorFap.ftl

  • preAssiagnRef.ftl

  • RoleAssign.ftl

  • SimpleData.ftl

  • SuccessInfo.ftl

  • TrxTemplate.ftl

  • unitAuth.ftl unitStruc.ftl

  • UploadImaging.ftl

  • UploadImagingAll.ftl

  • UploadMsgCata.ftl

  • userAndUnitFunc.ftl

  • ViewImaging.ftl

Example: Changing the L&F of CE

Example: Changing the L&F of CE

The CE user interface can be changed by modifying the files and parameters discussed in the previous chapters.

Changing the Header of the Logon Page

Do the following . . .
1. Design the image file for the header of the logon page using an image editing software. Make sure that the relevant image is saved as a JPG file.
2. Save the image file in the following directory: [WEB SERVER DRIVE]/Images
3. The change is reflected on the logon page of the system.

Changing the Body of the Logon Page

Do the following . . .
1. Design the image file for the body of the logon page using an image editing software. Make sure that the relevant image is saved as a PNG file.
Design the image file for the button on the logon page using an image editing software. Make sure that the relevant image is saved as a GIF file.
2. Save the image files in the following directory: [WEB SERVER DRIVE]/Images
3. The changes are reflected on the logon page of the system.

Changing the Header of the Landing Page

Do the following . . .
1. Design the image file for the header of the landing page using an image editing software. Make sure that the image is saved as a JPG file.
2. Save the image file in the following directory: [WEB SERVER DRIVE]/Images
3. The change is reflected on the landing page of the system

Changing the Body of the Landing Page

Do the following . . .
1. Design the image file for the body of the landing page using an image editing software. Make sure that the image is saved as a JPG file.
2. Save the image file in the following directory: [WEB SERVER DRIVE]/Images
3. The change is reflected on the landing page of the system
This is also reflected in all transaction processing and standing data functions.
This is also reflected in all the security functions.

Changing the Menu Style of the Landing Page

Do the following . . .
MODIFYING THE BACKROUND 1. Design the image file for the main menu of the system using an image editing software. Make sure that the image is saved as a JPG file.
2. Save the image file in the following directory: [WEB SERVER DRIVE]/Images
3. The change is reflected in the main menu of the system
MODIFYING THE STYLE OF THE FUNCTIONS IN THE MAIN MENU The style of functions in the main menu can also be changed as required. Access the Standard.css file. Add the relevant CSS codes to modify the border element for all the functions. This change is reflected in the list of functions in the main menu.

System JSP Files

The following table lists the currently used alias names and their corresponding system JSP files.

Alias File Name and Description
VascoGetChallengeNm ../screen/CE_VascoGetChallengeNm.jsp VASCO logon page
ReportGenerateSuccess ../screen/SYS_ReportGenerateSuccess.jsp Success page for report generation
SecuCatalog ../{BankGroup}/{CountryCode}/WEB/CATA/SYS_SecuCatalog.jsp Catalog page for the SECU and STAN modules
LoginToken ../screen/inputLoginToken.jsp Token logon page
AuthRulesMatrix ../{BankGroup}/{CountryCode}/WEB/SECU/SecuAuthMgr_Rules_Matrix.jsp Authorization Rule function screen (by Matrix)
ImgListView ../screen/CE_ImgListView.jsp Displays the document list and provides the onClick event when going over (mouseover) a document (e.g., child catalog in the Reports from the Back-office function)
GetTrxItem ../screen/SYS_GetNewItem.jsp New page for choosing a company (currently used in transaction modules)
TrxMainMenu ../screen/SYS_main_menu.jsp Transaction landing page
SecuMainMenu ../screen/SYS_security_menu.jsp Security landing page
BatchManageInit ../{BankGroup}/{CountryCode}/WEB/SCRN/BatchManageInit.jsp Batch Manager function screen
ClauseMain ../{BankGroup}/{CountryCode}/WEB/CLAUSE/ClauseMain.jsp Insert Clause dialog box (main screen)
ClauseContext ../{BankGroup}/{CountryCode}/WEB/CLAUSE/ClauseContext.jsp Used to show clause content in the Insert Clause dialog box
InqCUBK ../screen/SYS_InqCUBK.jsp Inquire CUBK screen
InquireTrxDetailList ../screen/SYS_CE_Inqire_TrxDetailList.jsp Transaction inquire history catalog screen
CETemplate ../screen/SYS_CE_Template.jsp Transaction template screen
CETemplateContent ../screen/SYS_CE_Template_Content.jsp Transaction template content screen
LogOff ../screen/SYS_LogOff.jsp System logoff screen (i.e., this is displayed when the session times out)
ImgSucc ../screen/SYS_ImgSucc.jsp Upload image success page
ViewGAPI ../screen/SYS_ViewGAPI.jsp Screen for viewing the GAPI message from CE to another system
GetUploadImaging ../screen/SYS_GetUploadImaging.jsp Upload image screen
MailReport /screen/mailReport.jsp Send e-mail screen
CompareEvent ../screen/SYS_CompareEvent.jsp Compare event screen
TitleCatalog ../{BankGroup}/{CountryCode}/WEB/CATA/SYS_TitleCatalog.jsp Inbox catalog screen
UserProfile ../screen/SYS_UserProfile.jsp Change user password screen
ResultSuccess ../screen/SYS_ResultSuccess.jsp Success page for normal transactions
ErrorPage /screen/errorPage.jsp Error JSP: This is the screen displayed when the system cannot retrieve the BU info from the session; it does not include the main menu. This is used in WSPageManager and not called by other functions.
LoginfailPage ../screen/loginfailPage.jsp Login failure screen
ResultError ../screen/SYS_ResultError.jsp Error page: If the transaction is unsuccessfully confirmed, the system displays this page to show the error.
ERROR ../screen/erro.jsp Replaced with “ResultError” in CEV2.1.0
CriteriaOfSecu ../screen/SYS_CriteriaSecu.jsp This is the pre-shown standalone criteria page for security functions. It is displayed when a file is specified for the “Criteria JSP file” catalog parameter and the “Show Position” is set to “Both”.
CriteriaOfTran ../screen/SYS_CriteriaTran.jsp This is the pre-shown standalone criteria page for transaction functions. It is displayed when a file is specified for the “Criteria JSP file” catalog parameter and the “Show Position” is set to “Both”.
InqViewDTLOpenWin ../screen/InqViewDTLOpenWin.jsp Used in Inquire History details and in comparing events

MainMenu.js

The MainMenu.js and other JS files are located in the following directory:

[WEB SERVER DRIVE]/JS

(Start of Code)

/**

* for generating main menu

*/

/**

* Data array in strArray

* [0 module][1 product id][2 name(?)][3 function id][4 function name][5 item id]

* [6 item name][7 product type(S or T)][8 new type][9 cata num][10 module description]

* [11 product description] [12 function description]

*/

//Global variables

var nNoOfFuncs = 0; // number of functions

var sSelectedProdId = “"; //Selected product id

var sSelectedFuncId = “"; //Selected function id

/**

* call showMainMenu() in the end of JSP

*/

function showMainMenu(){

try {

if (!window.strArray) {

showMsg(“The FAP is invalid.", “There was a problem login in.");

return;

}

//PRODUCT_ID is in catalog and trx

if (window.PRODUCT_ID && window.PRODUCT_ID.length > 0) {

sSelectedProdId = PRODUCT_ID;

}

//get function id for catalog and transaction screen

if (window.selFuncDesc && window.selFuncDesc.length > 0 && window.selFuncDesc != “null” && window.PRODUCT_ID) {

sSelectedFuncId = getFuncIdByFuncDesc(selFuncDesc)

}

var b = document.getElementById(“ProdMenu”);

if(b){ genMainMenu(b)}

}

catch (a) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, a)

}

}

var hiddenProdArray=[];

var hiddenFuncArray=[];

function inHiddenProdArray(b){

for(var a=0;a<hiddenProdArray.length;a++){

if(b==hiddenProdArray[a])

{return true}}return false}

function inHiddenFuncArray(d,e){

for(var b=0;b<hiddenFuncArray.length;b++)

{if(d==hiddenFuncArray[b][0])

{var c=hiddenFuncArray[b][1];

for(var a=0;a<c.length;a++){if(e==c[a])

{return true}}}}return false

}

function genMainMenu(b){

try {

if (!window.strArray) {

showMsg(“The FAP is invalid.", “There was a problem login in.");

return;

}

//init variable

if (LOGIN_NAME && LOGIN_NAME == “A”) {

isSEC = true;

}

else {

isSEC = false;

}

nNoOfFuncs = strArray.length;

genProdTable(b);

}

catch (a) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, a);

}

}

/**

* Generate product table

*

*/

function genProdTable(f){

try {

//drop product menu table

if (f.firstChild) {

f.removeChild(f.firstChild);

}

//create product menu table and append to product menu table cell

var b = document.createElement(“table”);

b.setAttribute(“id”, “ProdMenuTable”);

b.setAttribute(“cellspacing”, “0”);

b.setAttribute(“cellpadding”, “0”);

b.className = “ProdItem”;

f.appendChild(b);

//create product menu table tbody

var d = document.createElement(“tbody”);

d.setAttribute(“id”, “ProdMenuTableBody”);

b.appendChild(d);

var a = f.id;

//create product rows in product menu table

genProdRow(d, a)

}

catch (c) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, c);

}

}

/**

* Generate product rows

*/

function genProdRow(d, k){

try {

var a = new Array();

var p = new Array();

for (var h = 0; h < nNoOfFuncs; h++) {

var r = strArray[h][1];

var g = strArray[h][11];

if (!p.in_array(g)) {

a.push(r);

p.push(g);

}

}

//add product row

var c = p.length;

for (var f = 0; f < c; f++) {

if(inHiddenProdArray(a[f])){continue}

var q = document.createElement(“tr”);

var b = “row_” + a[f];

q.setAttribute(“id”, b);

var l = document.createElement(“td”);

var o = “cell_” + a[f];

l.setAttribute(“id”, o);

var m = document.createElement(“a”);

m.setAttribute(“id”, a[f]);

m.setAttribute(“pid”, k);

m.href = “#";

//set class to SelectedProdLink

if (a[f] == sSelectedProdId) {

m.className = “SelectedProdLink”

}

else {

m.className = “ProdLink”

}

m.innerHTML = p[f];

m.onclick = getProdIdOnClick;

l.appendChild(m);

q.appendChild(l);

d.appendChild(q);

//show selected product functions

if (sSelectedProdId.length > 0 && sSelectedProdId == a[f]) {

genProdFunc(d, sSelectedProdId);

}

}

}

catch (e) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, e)

}

}

/**

* Generate produc functions table

*/

function genProdFunc(k, h){

try {

var m = h;

var c = new Array();

//function id under this product

for (var g = 0; g < nNoOfFuncs; g++) {

if (strArray[g][1] == m) {

var l = strArray[g][3];

c.push(l)

}

}

var b = document.createElement(“tr”);

k.appendChild(b);

var d = document.createElement(“td”);

d.setAttribute(“id”, “selectedSubMenu”);

d.style.paddingRight = “0px”;

d.style.paddingLeft = “0px”;

d.style.paddingBottom = “0px”;

d.style.paddingTop = “0px”;

b.appendChild(d);

//product function table

var f = document.createElement(“table”);

f.setAttribute(“id”, “ProdFuncTable”);

f.setAttribute(“cellspacing”, “0”);

f.setAttribute(“cellpadding”, “0”);

f.className = “FuncItem”;

d.appendChild(f);

//product function table body

var a = document.createElement(“tbody”);

a.setAttribute(“id”, “ProdFuncTableBody”);

f.appendChild(a);

//generate function rows

genFuncRow(m, c, a)

}

catch (j) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, j)

}

}

/**

* Generate produc function rows

*/

function genFuncRow(s, b, a){

try {

var l= new Array();

var c = new Array();

//get func desc under this product

for (var g = 0; g < nNoOfFuncs; g++) {

var h = strArray[g][5];

var q = strArray[g][12];

if (strArray[i][1] == s) {

l.push(h);

c.push(q);

}

}

//add product row

var o = b.length;

for (var f = 0; f < o; f++) {

if(inHiddenFuncArray(s,b[f])){continue}

var p = document.createElement(“tr”);

var n = “funcrow_” + b[f];

p.setAttribute(“id”, n);

var d = document.createElement(“td”);

var r = “funccell_” + b[f];

d.style.paddingRight = “0px”;

d.style.paddingLeft = “14px”;

d.setAttribute(“id”, r);

var k = document.createElement(“a”);

k.setAttribute(“id”, b[f]);

k.href = “#";

if (b[f] == sSelectedFuncId) {

k.className = “SelectedFuncLink”

}

else {

k.className = “FuncLink”

}

k.innerHTML = c[f];

k.onclick = getFuncIdOnClick;

d.appendChild(k);

p.appendChild(d);

a.appendChild(p);

}

}

catch (m) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, m)

}

}

/**

* Get product id for product onclick and then generate product menu

*/

function getProdIdOnClick(c){

try {

var i = getEvtTarget(c);

var a = i.id;

if (sSelectedProdId == a) {

var f = document.getElementById(“selectedSubMenu”);

var b = f.style.display;

if (“none” == b) {

f.style.display = “block”

}

else {

f.style.display = “none”

}

}

else {

var g = sSelectedProdId;

sSelectedProdId = a;

var d = i.getAttribute(“pid”);

genProdTable(document.getElementById(d))

}

}

catch (h) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, h)

}

}

/**

* Get function id for function onclick and then call funcItemClick()

*/

function getFuncIdOnClick(a){

try {

var g = getEvtTarget(a);

var c = g.id;

sSelectedFuncId = c;

//click function on main menu in the trx, show confirmation msg first

if (!isSEC && (window.SYS_FUNCTION_NAME && window.SYS_FUNCTION_NAME.length > 0)) {

var b = false;

if (SYS_FUNCTION_NAME.indexOf(“View”) != -1) {

b = true

}

if (b || isRptFunc) {

_funcItemClick(sSelectedFuncId)

}

else {

var d = window.confirm(“Data will not be saved if you proceed.");

if (d) {

_funcItemClick(sSelectedFuncId)

}

}

}

else {

//disable fields if it is CSX to CE msg func

if (window.ITEM_ID) {

if (ITEM_ID == “STPDemerge”) {

var h = document.forms.MAINFORM

}

}

_funcItemClick(sSelectedFuncId)

}

}

catch (f) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, f)

}

}

/**

* Get function id by function description

*/

function getFuncIdByFuncDesc(b){

try {

for (var c = 0; c < strArray.length; c++) {

if (strArray[c][12] == b && strArray[c][1] == PRODUCT_ID) {

var a = strArray[c][3];

return a

}

}

}

catch (d) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, d);

}

}

/**

* Get function description by function id

*/

function getFuncDescByFuncId(b){

try {

for (var c = 0; c < nNoOfFuncs; c++) {

if (strArray[c][3] == b) {

var a = strArray[c][12];

return a;

}

}

}

catch (d) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, d)

}

}

/**

* Get function description by function name

*/

function getFuncDescByFuncNm(b){

try {

for (var c = 0; c < nNoOfFuncs; c++) {

if (strArray[c][4] == b) {

var a = strArray[c][12];

return a;

}

}

}

catch (d) {

showExcpt(“MainMenu”, d)

}

};

PART II:
CE WIDGET FRAMEWORK

Introduction to CE Widgets

  • Widget Overview and Prerequisites

  • The Initial CE Landing Page with widgets

  • General Widget Parameter Settings

Widget Overview and Prerequisites

Widgets

A widget is a small application that can be installed and run within a web page by an end-user. Occupying only a minor portion of a web page, a widget performs a basic functionality. Widgets often take the form of on-screen programs such as calculators and event countdowns.

In CE Version 3.0 and higher, 12 types of widgets are supported. These standard (native) widgets are:

  • Calculator

  • Calendar Events

  • Criteria Search

  • Dashboard

  • Exchange Rate

  • Main Menu

  • Notice

  • Quick Access

  • Recent Functions

  • Summary

  • Upload Message

  • Welcome

  • Statistics

NOTE: The Notice widget is formerly called Notification widget in versions prior to CE Version 3.2.0.

With this Widget functionality in CE:

  • The consultant or developer can:

  • import a Widget list into the CE application

  • design the look and feel of the CE application with widgets

  • The end-user can customize the tabs and widgets of the CE application. The specific attributes of a widget can be modified as well.

  • Security FAP and DAP checks are inherited from the current CE entitlements.

  • A project team can build its own special widgets and plug it into this framework.

NOTE: CSWidgets refers to the widget standard of China Systems.

The CSWidgets widget standard supports most of the features in JSR168 and JSR286. If it is required to show the CE widgets in the bank’s portlet server, major services for the bank’s portlet server can be provided. Moreover, the CSWidgets standard matches the JSR168 and JSR286 portlet standards.

Figure 9. 1 Example: CE Design Layout with Widgets

Prerequisites

To support widgets on the CE landing page, including the Personalize link that is used for customizing the tabs and widgets, modify the following file:

[PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\SYST\sys_screens.xml

  • Change the TrxMainMenu setting:
From
<SCREEN> <ALIAS>TrxMainMenu</ALIAS> <DESC>Trx main menu</DESC> <JSPFILE>../screen/SYS_main_menu.jsp</JSPFILE> <TMPLFILE>../Templates/SYS_Template.jsp</TMPLFILE> </SCREEN>
To
<SCREEN> <ALIAS>TrxMainMenu</ALIAS> <DESC>Trx main menu</DESC> <JSPFILE>../screen/widgetMain.jsp</JSPFILE> <TMPLFILE>../Templates/WGT_Template.jsp</TMPLFILE> </SCREEN>
  • Add this setting:
<SCREEN> <ALIAS>CustomizeWidget</ALIAS> <DESC>Customize Widget</DESC> <JSPFILE>../screen/widgetCust.jsp</JSPFILE> <TMPLFILE>../Templates/WGT_Template.jsp</TMPLFILE> </SCREEN>

After making these modifications, restart the application server.

The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets

In CE versions that utilize the widget functionality, the browser provides default screen elements. This includes standard or native widgets.

NOTE: A function (e.g., Add Personalize) may be added in the security module that is used to define available widgets and assign default widgets to be used based on bank and regional country code. Refer to the CE Security and System Maintenance Functions documentation for more information on this function.

Figure 9. 2 Initial CE Widget Landing Page

Screen Elements

Initial access of the CE browser provides the following default screen elements:

  • Header section

  • Home tab

  • Widgets

  • Footer section

Header Section

Aside from the China Systems logo, the header section of the browser shows the following links.

Figure 9. 3 Header Section

Link Description
(Current User) Clicking on the link that stands for the logged-on user displays a window through which the user password and e-mail can be changed. Refer to Chapter Three: Change User Profile discussion for instructions on changing the password and the e-mail of the logged-on user.
(Languages) Click on the relevant icon to switch to the corresponding language it represents. NOTE: The languages available are based on multi-language settings. The relevant flag images are added in the following folder – [CEWeb.war folder]\Images\cou – and their corresponding methods added in the BankBanner.lbi file contained in this path: [CEWeb.war folder]\include Refer to the CE Multi-language manual for more details on multi-language settings.
Personalize This is used for customizing the tabs and widgets to be displayed on the CE browser. NOTE: This link is discussed in detail in the widget sections of this document.
Help This link is currently not used.
Sign Out This is used for logging out of the system.

Home Tab

On first accessing the CE browser, a default tab is provided: Home. The Home tab contains two widgets: Main Menu and Welcome.

Figure 9. 4 Default Tab: Home

Other tabs, as well as widgets, can be added to the system as required.

NOTE: For details on adding tabs, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Basic CE Widget Operations > Adding Tabs on the Landing Page

Widgets

The default tab of the CE system, Home, contains these widgets: Main Menu and Welcome.

Figure 9. 5 Default Widgets: Main Menu and Welcome

Other widgets, as well as tabs, can be added to the system as required.

NOTE: For details on adding widgets, refer to the following discussion in this chapter: Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Footer Section

The footer section displays the copyright information of the CE system, as well as links that point to information about China Systems.

Figure 9. 6 Footer Section

Basic CE Widget Operations

With the initial and default widget settings in CE, the end-user can perform the following on the CE landing page:

  • Display specific widgets

  • Remove specific widgets

  • Add tabs

These are configured through the Personalize page of the system.

NOTE: The Personalize page is also referred to as the Page Builder.

Displaying Widgets

The CE landing page may contain multiple tabs. The layout of a tab can support:

  • A maximum of three columns; and

  • Each column can contain as many widget instances as required.

    By default, the system provides the Home tab with the Main Menu and Welcome widget instances.

NOTE: Widgets of the same type are called instances of that widget.

To add a widget on the relevant tab:

Do the following . . .
1. Log on the CE system as an Operator user. The CE landing page is displayed.
2. Click on the Personalize link.
3. The Personalize page is displayed. On the left section is the Product Services panel. This lists all the available widgets. The right section displays the available tabs and their corresponding widget instances. Click on the tab to which the widget instance is to be added. Relevant sections are allocated for cross-column widgets. EXAMPLE: The Main Menu and Welcome widgets have been added to the Home tab. NOTE: Refer to the Adjusting Widget Layouts discussion in this chapter for more details on cross-column widgets.
NOTE: The types of widgets that are made available on the Product Services depend on the role of the logged-on user. A widget type is assigned to specific user roles.
4. From the Product Services panel, click and drag the widget to the right section and towards the relevant tab. EXAMPLE: The Notification widget is to be added to the Home tab.
5. An instance of this widget is now added to the tab. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
NOTE: Depending on the setting configured for it, a widget may or may not be utilized on the same tab multiple times. (For settings, refer to the following discussion in this chapter: General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings > Procedure). A disabled widget name on the Product Services panel indicates that it can no longer be added to the current tab (through drag-and-drop). As long as the widget name is enabled, then it can be added multiple times to the current tab: multiple instances of this widget can be displayed and utilized on that tab. EXAMPLE: Given that: 1) There are two tabs: Home and Test; 2) The Welcome widget has been defined to be utilized only once; 3) The Main Menu widget has been defined to be utilized multiple times; and 4) The Home tab already contains a Main Menu widget instance. Do the following: Access the Home tab. The tab already contains an instance of the Main Menu widget. On the Product Services panel, the Main Menu widget name remains enabled. This indicates that another or more instances of the Main Menu widget can be added to the tab. Drag and drop a Welcome widget instance to the Home tab. The Welcome widget name on the Product Services panel becomes disabled. This indicates that the system cannot allow another instance of the Welcome widget to be utilized on the Home tab. Access the Test tab. The Welcome widget instance on the Product Services panel becomes enabled. Drag and drop a Welcome widget instance to the Test tab. The Welcome widget name on the Product Services panel becomes disabled. This indicates that the system cannot allow another instance of the Welcome widget to be utilized on the Test tab. Drag and drop two instances of the Main Menu widget to the Test tab. The widget name remains enabled on the Product Services panel. Tabs: Home and Test Home tab Test tab:
NOTE: The arrangement of widgets can be changed by dragging and dropping the widgets to the relevant positions.
7. The system returns to the landing page. The added widget instance is shown on the relevant tab.

Adjusting Widget Layouts

The CE system supports a maximum of 4 widget columns.

It also provides the feature to set the width of a widget to occupy 2 columns on the screen, while maintaining the set column layout for other widgets. This allows widgets that have more details and be more readable and accessible.

If a widget is set to occupy two columns, it is called a Cross Column Widget.

To enable cross column widgets, the following items must be configured:

  • widget.xml of the relevant widget.

  • TWO_COLUMNS_WIDGET system parameter

  • Widget JSP and JS files

    • NOTE: For lower CE versions, a maximum of 3 widget columns is supported.

Widget.xml File

To enable cross column widgets, the acrossColumn attribute must be modified or added to the corresponding widget.xml file of the relevant widget.

NOTE: Once the value of the acrossColumn attribute is set to Y and the widget is added to the cross column section, it may not be reverted back to a normal widget until the acrossColumn attribute is set to N and the application server is restarted.

Example:

<iw:itemSet id="attributes”>

<iw:item id="acrossColumn” alias="acrossColumn” lang=”” readOnly="false” value="Y”/>

</iw:itemSet>

TWO_COLUMNS_WIDGET System Parameter

This parameter is used to define whether the width of a widget is to be automatically adjusted or to be retained to its default setting.

If the value of this parameter is set to TRUE, the system automatically adjusts the width of each column to occupy 50% of the browser page width. This applies if the widgets are set to occupy only two columns on the browser page.

If the value of this parameter is set to FALSE, the width of each column remains at 33% of the browser page width, regardless if the defined layout is two or three columns.

Layout.jsp

The layout.jsp file is used to define the columns on the landing page where widgets are to be arranged.

This is also used to define the location of cross column section. Different sets of codes are provided to display the cross column section either on the left side or right side of the page.

NOTE: Refer to the Setting Widget Columns discussion in Chapter 23 for more information on widget column settings.

To display the cross column section on the right side of the page for 3 column widget setting, the layout.jsp file must have the following contents:

<%@ taglib uri=”/LFTAGS” prefix="widget” %> <%@ taglib uri = “/MLGTAG” prefix = “MLG”%> <widget:resource type="layout” path="column3.css”/> <% // //CEV2-04-01-12 harry.wang %> <div id="layoutContainers” class="csLayoutContainers”> <div id="com_cs_widgets_layout_R1C3” class="component-container layoutCol csLayoutColumn3 oneColumn”> <widget:wrappers cellId="com_cs_widgets_layout_R1C3”/> </div> <div class="line”> <div id="com_cs_widgets_layout_R1C4” class="component-container layoutCol4 csLayoutColumn4 twoColumn”> <div id="call-word” align="center” style="font-size:30px;color:gray;position:relative;">Please drag the cross - column widget to here. </div> <widget:wrappers cellId="com_cs_widgets_layout_R1C4”/> </div> <div class="line2”> <div id="com_cs_widgets_layout_R1C1” class="component-container layoutCol csLayoutColumn1 oneColumn”> <widget:wrappers cellId="com_cs_widgets_layout_R1C1”/> </div> <div id="com_cs_widgets_layout_R1C2” class="component-container layoutColM csLayoutColumn2 oneColumn”> <widget:wrappers cellId="com_cs_widgets_layout_R1C2”/> </div> </div> </div> </div> <%@ page import="com.cs.core.cache.CacheSYSHelper”%> <%@ page import="com.cs.core.utility.StringUtil”%> <%String twoColumnsWidget = CacheSYSHelper.getSysParam(“TWO_COLUMNS_WIDGET”); if(StringUtil.isEmpty(twoColumnsWidget)){ twoColumnsWidget = “FALSE”; } %> <script type="text/javascript”> //CEV2-04-01-12 harry.wang s $(document).ready(function(){ var TCWidget=”<%=twoColumnsWidget%>”; if($("#divCenter”).children().length == 1){ $("#call-word”).remove(); $(".layoutCol4”).css(“border”,“0px”); //$(".layoutCol4”).css(“min-height”,“0px”); if($(".layoutCol4”).children().length== 0){ $(".layoutCol4”).css(“display”,“none”); } $(".csLayoutColumn3”).each(function(){ if($(this).children().length== 0 && TCWidget == “TRUE”){ $(this).css(“width”,“0%"); $(this).siblings().css(“width”,“100%"); }else{ $(this).css(“width”,“33%"); $(this).siblings().css(“width”,“66%"); } }); }else{ $(".csLayoutColumn4”).each(function(){ if($(this).children().length > 1){ $($(this).children().get(0)).hide(); } }); } }); //CEV2-04-01-12 harry.wang e </script>

Column3.css

The column3.css file contains Cascading Style Sheets (CSS) codes that are used to define the format and layout of the html elements that are defined in the layout.jsp file.

To enable cross column widgets, this file must have the following contents:

.widgetMain { background: none repeat scroll 0 0 #FFFFFF; border: 0 none; padding: 10px 0 0; min-height: 600px; position: relative; height:auto !important; display: inline-block; width:100%; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers{ overflow: visible; padding: 0; display: inline-block; width: 100%; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .component-container { float: left; display: inline; position: relative; box-sizing:border-box; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .component-container.csLayoutColumn1, .component-container.csLayoutColumn4{ padding-left: 5px; } /*.widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .layoutCol, .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .layoutColM { width: 33%; min-height: 600px; height:auto ; }*/ #loading.tb.lt{ display: none; } #loading .msgp .bar .rate.ltr{ width: 33%; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .component-container.csLayoutColumn1, .component-container.csLayoutColumn2{ width: 50%; min-height: 600px; height:auto; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .component-container.csLayoutColumn3{ width: 33%; min-height: 600px; height:auto; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .layoutCol4 { width: 100%; min-height: 120px; height:auto; border:1px dashed #C0C0C0; } .line{ float:left; display: inline; width:66%; } .line2{ float:left; display:block; width:100%; }
