this.getStructTab(tab.id).name = oriTabName; var item = $("#tab-“+tab.id); item.text(oriTabName); var layout = this.struct.layouts[tab.id]; var lt = $.CSWidget.getLayout(null,tab.id); for(cell in layout){ var widgets = layout[cell]; for(var i=0;i<widgets.length;i++){ var widget = widgets[i]; var wid = widget.id; var inst = lt.getInstance(wid); var idesc = inst.iContext.getiDescriptor(); var attrs = inst.iContext.getiWidgetAttributes(); if(idesc.getChanges().changes.length || attrs.getChanges().changes.length){ lt.revertInstance(wid,false); } } } } var selected = deftab != null?$("#tab-“+deftab.id) :$(".widgetTab[role=tab]:first”); var tabs = $.CSWidget.getTabs(); tabs.setCurrentTab(selected); var curr = tabs.getCurrentTab(); $(“input[name=tabName]",".layout-config”).val(curr.name); this.struct = $.CSWidget.clone(this.initStruct); $(".layout”,$.CSWidget.Constants.layoutRoot).remove(); var layout = $.CSWidget.getLayout(); layout.onLoad(); }, onItemSetChanged:function(evt){ if(“mode” == evt.changes.id || “windowState” == evt.changes.id){ return; } var pw = $.CSWidget.getPersonalize(); pw.setModifiedState(true); }, setModifiedState:function(){ this.saved = false; $(".save-button”,".main-toolbar”).button(“option”,{ disabled:false, highlight:true }); var pw = this; var labels = “widget.personalize.labels”; $(".message-bar”).messageBar({ text:$.CSWidget.getLocalizedItemValue(labels,“msg.notsaved”), actions:[{ text:$.CSWidget.getLocalizedItemValue(labels,“msg.act.save”), action:function(ui,bar){ pw.onStructSave(function(){ $(".save-button”,".main-toolbar”).button(“option”,{ disabled:true, highlight:false }); }); } },{ text:$.CSWidget.getLocalizedItemValue(labels,“msg.act.discard”), action:function(ui,bar){ pw.revertLayout(); $(".save-button”,".main-toolbar”).button(“option”,{ disabled:true, highlight:false }); bar.messageBar(“option”,“display”,“hide”); } }] }); } });

CSWidget.js

The CSWidget.js file contains JavaScript codes that handle the behavior of widgets.

To enable cross column widgets, the following items must be added to the Constants block:

  • layoutCols1:".twoColumn”

  • layoutCols2:".oneColumn”

Example:

Constants:{ navTabRoot:".widgetNavTabs”, layoutRoot:".widgetMain”, layoutBody:".csLayoutContainers”, layoutCols:".component-container”, //CEV2-04-01-12 harry.wang s layoutCols1:".twoColumn”, layoutCols2:".oneColumn”, //CEV2-04-01-12 harry.wang e widgetRoot:".component-control”, widgetHead:".decoration-titlebar”, widgetBody:".csWidgetBody”, widgetFoot:".decoration-toolbar”, actMenuIcon:".cs-mode-menu”, placeholder:“widget-placeholder”, widgetsPool:".widgetsPool”, settingBar:".settingBar”, initMode:“view”, personalize:false, personalizeBtn:".personalizeBtn”, TabSource:"../widgets/framework/scripts/Tabs.js”, ActionMenuSource:"../widgets/framework/scripts/WidgetActionMenu.js”, lang:null, SUPPORTED_IE:[“6.0”,“7.0”,“8.0”,“9.0”,“10.0”] } } });
Do the following . . .
Configuring the widget.xml File 1. Open the corresponding widget.xml file of the widget to be set as a cross-column. This file is located in the [Parameter Drive]:\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\[widget name] folder.
2. Set the value of the acrossColumn attribute to Y. Once done, save the changes made to the file.
Modifying the TWO_COLUMNS_WIDGET System Parameter 3. Log on to the CE Utility as a super administrator user.
4. Run the System Parameters function from the Parameter Manage function group.
5. Select the TWO_COLUMNS_WIDGET parameter, and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
6. The Modify Parameter Config window is displayed. Set the Parameter Value to TRUE. Once done, click on the Save button.
XML GENERATION: Log on to the CE Utility as an operator user.
Run the XML Generator function and select System Parameter. Mark the Security System Parameter option.
The XML file for system parameters is generated in this folder: [Parameter Drive]:\CE_SYS\SYST\sys_para.xml
Modifying JSP and JS Files 7. Open the layout.jsp file. This file is located in the CEWeb.war:\widgets\framework\layouts\column3 folder.
8. Specify the required information. Once done, save the changes made to the file. NOTE: Refer to Chapter 9: Layout.jsp for the required contents of the layout.jsp file.
9. Open the column3.css file. This file is located in the CEWeb.war:\widgets\framework\layouts\column3 folder.
10. Specify the required details. Once done, save the changes made to the file. NOTE: Refer to Chapter 9: Column3.css for the required contents of the column3.css file.
11. Open the Personalize.js file. This file is located in the CEWeb.war:\widgets\framework\personalize folder.
12. Specify the required details. Once done, save the changes made to the file. NOTE: Refer to Chapter 9: Personalize.js for the required contents of the Personalize.js file.
13. Open the CSWidget.js file. This file is located in the CEWeb.war:\widgets\framework\scripts folder.
14. Specify the required details. Once done, save the changes made to the file. NOTE: Refer to Chapter 9: CSWidget.js for the required contents of the CSWidget.js file.
Application Server Restart After configuring all required parameters, the application server must be restarted.
Adjusting Widget Layouts 1. Log on the CE system as an Operator user. The CE landing page is displayed.
2. Click on the Personalize link that is located on the top right corner of the page.
3. The Personalize page is displayed. On the left section is the Product Services panel. This lists all the available widgets. The right section displays the available tabs and their corresponding widget instances. Click on the tab to which the widget instance is to be added. The cross column section is displayed. NOTE: The position of the cross column section is determined based on the settings defined in the layout.jsp file. Refer to Chapter 9: Layout.jsp.
4. From the Product Services panel, click and drag the widget to the right section and towards the cross column section of the relevant tab. EXAMPLE: The Dashboard widget is to be added to the Home tab, and is set as a cross column widget.
5. An instance of this widget is now added to the tab. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
NOTE: The arrangement of widgets can be changed by dragging and dropping the widgets to the relevant positions.
7. The system returns to the landing page. The added widget instance is shown on the relevant tab.
NOTE: Use the Column Number field to specify the number of widget columns that are to be used. Refer to the Setting Widget Columns discussion in Chapter 23 for more details on widget columns.

Removing Widgets

To remove a widget from the relevant tab on the landing page:

Do the following . . .
1. Log on to the CE system as an Operator user. The CE landing page is displayed.
2. Click on the Personalize link.
3. The Personalize page is displayed. On the left section is the Product Services panel. This lists all the available widget (or widget instances). The right section displays the available tabs and their corresponding widget instances. Click on the tab that contains the widget instance to be removed. EXAMPLE: The Main Menu, Welcome, and Quick Access widgets have been added to the Home tab.
4. Each widget instance is provided with a menu.
Open this menu and click on the Remove option to delete the widget instance. EXAMPLE: The Quick Access widget is to be removed from the Home tab.
5. The widget instance has now been deleted. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page. The deleted widget instance is no longer shown on the relevant tab.

Adding Tabs on the Landing Page

A tab may contain several widgets. It may take some time, however, to load the page if a tab contains too many widgets. Multiple tabs, each containing a set of widgets, enable the system to load all the screen elements more efficiently.

The system provides a default tab: Home. To add a tab on the landing page:

Do the following . . .
1. Log on the CE system as an Operator user. The CE landing page is displayed.
2. Click on the Personalize link.
3. The Personalize page is displayed. On the left section is the Product Services panel. This lists all the available widgets. The right section displays the available tabs and their corresponding widget instances. EXAMPLE: The available and current tab is the Home tab.
4. Click on the Add New Tab button.
NOTE: The Show Grid button is used for displaying the grid on the screen in order to better view the alignment of the widgets.
5. A new tab is shown. Specify the name of this new tab in the field provided.
6. The specified name is reflected on the actual tab. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
A tab is added, labeled with the name previously specified. Arrange the widgets to be included in each tab and save the changes made. NOTE: For adding a widget to a new tab, refer to this previous discussion: Displaying Widgets.
7. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
8. The system returns to the landing page.
The new tab is now added to the landing page. Click on the name of the new tab to access this tab.
The new tab’s page is then displayed.
NOTE: To rename a tab, access it on the Personalize page. Specify a new name in the Name field provided and save the setting.
To delete a tab, access it on the Personalize page. Either click on the X symbol or click on the Close button. Save the setting.
To arrange the order of tabs, go to the Personalize page. Drag the tab to the required position and save the setting.
In case the tabs are not properly aligned horizontally, modify the following file: CEWeb.war\theme\default\widgets\tabs.css. Comment out the display code.

General Widget Parameter Settings

All widget types require a profile definition. This profile definition can also be used for creating another widget of the same primary attributes.

With some widgets, additional or advanced settings are required.

NOTE: The specific settings that apply to a particular widget type are discussed in the chapter dedicated to that widget.

Widget Profile Settings

The Widget profile is defined through the Widget Maintain function.

Configuration

Define the following details in the Widget Profile window.

Figure 9. 7 Widget Profile Window

Field Field Description
Widget Name Specify the unique key of the widget. In configuring any of the 12 basic CE widgets, the following exact names must be followed: Calculator CalendarEvents CriteriaSearch Dashboard ExchangeRate MainMenu Notification QuickAccess RecentFunction Summary UploadMessage WelcomeBox NOTE: A widget profile that is based on any of the 12 CE standard widgets can be created. This functionality is done through the Extend Definition File option. Refer to the Widget Definition File Extension discussion in this chapter for more details.
Description Provide the description of the widget. This becomes the default name of the widget in the Frame Work list section in the Widget Setting tab of the Widget Maintain function window.
Widget Type This is currently not used. Nonetheless, make sure that the Global option is selected.
Version Specify the version of the widget. This is used for information and tracking purposes in case the widget is updated in the future.
System Role Assign the user role for the widget: select the kinds of users to which the widget is to be made available. The user roles are: Super Officer Bank Administrator Bank Operator Customer Administrator Customer Operator At least one user role must be selected. Otherwise, it cannot be used by any user once this setting is synchronized with the database. Upon synchronization (through the Synchronize to DB button), the widget details defined here are going to override the original settings in the database. NOTE: These roles are stored in the SEC_WIDGET_RIGHTS table. The values are 0, for Super Officer; 1 for Customer Administrator; 2, for Customer Operator; 3 for Bank Administrator; and 4, for Bank Operator.
Status This indicates whether or not the widget can be used. Select the Active option. NOTE: The Inactive option is currently not used.

Procedure

To configure the Welcome widget…
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
NOTE: The Widget Profile tab also provides the following buttons: Synchronize to DB Import Export as SQL
Synchronize to DB button is used for inserting the widget profiles to the database. The new widget settings defined in this function override the original data in the database. This is used in the testing environment only.
The Import button is used for importing a default XML configuration file for some widget profiles. Note that: Only the profile details are imported; and The XML file may contain, or may be edited to contain, multiple widget profiles through the addition of <widget> nodes. Duplicate widget instances cannot be imported.
The Export as SQL button is used to generate and export the SQL commands for creating these widget profiles to an SQL file. The SQL file can be run in the production environment in order to import the widget data saved in the testing database.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget profile and click on the Save button.
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings. NOTE: Once created, the widget profile is inserted into the CEMETA.ECD_WIDGET_PROFILE table. When the Synchronize to DB button is clicked, the profile is inserted into the CEUSER.SEC_WIDGET and CEUSER.SEC_WIDGET_RIGHTS tables.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile (i.e., extension). Refer to this section: Widget Definition File Extension
9. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\WelcomeBox\widget.xml
10. The content of the imported file is shown on the configuration window. Check or modify the settings as required.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
11. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\[WIDGET NAME]\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile. EXAMPLE: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\WelcomeBox\widget.xml

NOTE: The other (non-profile) settings that are specific to a particular widget type are discussed in the chapter dedicated to that widget.

Widget Definition File Extension

Any one of the 12 standard CE widgets can be used to create a new widget profile that is to have the same attributes.

EXAMPLE:

The Summary widget is used for viewing and accessing one type of records only (via catalog). The widget must be configured on Edit mode in order to display records from other particular catalogs.

For easier and faster access to other types of records, additional Summary widgets, using the attributes of the standard Summary widget, can be created.

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting
3. Through the Widget Profile tab, create a new widget profile. The name must be different from any of the 12 standard CE widgets. EXAMPLE: Widget Name: SummaryEXLC Description: Summary for Export LC NOTE: Widget profile configuration is detailed in this section: General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. Mark the Extend Definition File option. From the accompanying dropdown list that is then enabled, select the standard widget which attributes are to be applied to the new widget. EXAMPLE: Extend Definition File: Summary NOTE: The Import Definition File option is used for importing the settings of a specific widget XML configuration file. Refer to: Widget Profile Settings
9. The settings defined for this standard widget are shown on the configuration window.
10. Change the description.
Make sure that the idescriptor tag is set to the defined description of the new widget. EXAMPLE: New widget description: Summary for Export LC
11. When done with the modifications, click on the Save button and close the window.
12. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the updated content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: WIDGET PROFILE Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\[WIDGET NAME]\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile. EXAMPLE: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\SummaryEXLC\widget.xml
13. Proceed with the other parameter settings required of the new widget. EXAMPLE: For the new SummaryEXLC widget, additional settings are required in the Advance Setting sub-tab of the Widget Setting tab. NOTE: Refer to the settings of the standard widget. There are separate chapters for each widget type. In this example, the standard widget is the Summary widget. Refer to Chapter Nineteen.
XML GENERATION: ADVANCED WIDGET SETTINGS Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML files are generated on this path: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\[WIDGET NAME] EXAMPLE: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\SummaryEXLC
The following file is also updated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\framework\extension-widgets.xml. NOTE: Make sure to clear the browser history and restart the server.
14. On the CE browser, access the Personalize page.
15. The new widget profile, created based on an existing profile (i.e., extension), is now included in the Product Services list. Use or configure the new widget accordingly.
Use or configure the new widget accordingly. NOTE: The CSS file to be applied to the widget is copied in this directory: CEWeb.war\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\[WIDGET NAME].

Other Widget Settings

Widget Action Popup Setting

The WIDGET_ACTION_POPUP security parameter is used to control whether the system pops up a new window when a widget hyperlink or button is clicked. The following is an example of how the system displays the relevant screen when this this parameter is set to TRUE.

EXAMPLE:

In the Dashboard widget, click on the View Import LC link. The View Import LC screen is displayed on a popup window:

In the Criteria Search widget, select the Import Letters of Credit – Authorise Transaction option from the Search For dropdown field and click on the Search button. The Authorise Transaction screen is displayed on a popup window:

RTL Settings

The RTL security parameter is used to change how widgets, transaction functions, and error messages are displayed on the CE page: certain elements are re-arranged from right to left.

For widgets –

  • The hyperlinks follow this order – Sign Out, Help, Personalize, [User Name] – instead of: [User Name], Personalize, Help, and Sign Out.

  • The Title and Description elements, when personalizing a widget, are right-aligned.

  • The functions from these widgets are right-aligned: Main Menu and its Search tool, Quick Access, and Recent Functions.

  • The descriptions are displayed on the right: Upload Message, Welcome, Criteria Search,

  • Calendar Events: The weekends and weekdays are displayed from right to left.

  • The elements are reversed: Exchange Rate (rates first, then the currencies), Summary, Notice.

For transaction functions:

  • The tabs and buttons are displayed in reversed order.

  • The field descriptions are displayed on the right.

For error messages:

  • The error messages are right-aligned.

To enable this right-to-left style for widgets:

Do the following . . .
1. As a Super Administrator user, run the System Parameters function from the Parameter Manage function group of the CE Utility.
2. Set the RTL system parameter value to: dir=’rtl’.
3. As an Operator user, run the XML Generator function from the Maintenance function group.
4. In the Web Server tab, double-click on System Parameter and select the following options in the window that is displayed: Security System Parameter System Session Data Click on the Save button.
5. Open the widget JS file found in this path: [WEB SERVER DRIVE]\ widgets\framework\scripts\CSWidget.js Add the codes in red font. NOTE: Refer to the Web Server JSP and JS File Modification section for the complete list of JSP and JS files that require modification to enable the RTL feature across the system.
Web Server JSP and JS File Modification To enable the RTL feature across the system, certain codes in the following JSP and JS files in the CE Web Server Drive must be modified. Specific Widget Settings

Some widget types require:

  • Advanced settings in the Widget Maintain function in the CE Utility

  • Settings in another CE Utility function (e.g., Notification function)

  • Prerequisite products and functions (e.g., Notification View and Label products)

These specific settings that apply only to particular widget types are discussed in their respective chapters.

The Calculator Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Calculator widget is a tool for basic calculation operations.

Figure 10. 1 The Calculator Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Calculator widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Calculator Widget

Parameter Settings

The parameter settings for the Calculator widget are configured in the Widget Maintain function.

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget. Make sure that the Widget Name is set to: Calculator. Click on the Save button. NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
9. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Calculator\widget.xml
10. The content of the imported file is shown on the configuration window. Check or modify the settings as required.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
11. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Calculator\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.

Browser Settings

Before using the Calculator widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Calculator widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Calculator Widget

To use the Calculator widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Calculator widget.
2. Use the Calculator widget accordingly.
NOTE: The Calculator widget provides a menu containing the Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options.

Changing the Calculator Widget Properties

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Calculator widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Calculator window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Calculator window provides a menu with the Remove, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options.
4. Modify the Calculator title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Calculator widget reflects the new title and description.

The Calendar Events Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter SEttings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Calendar Events widget, aside from showing basic calendar information, provides the following functionalities:

  • Weekends and holidays are highlighted for easy identification.

  • Dates with events are appropriately marked with flags.

  • The types of events to be utilized by the widget can be defined.

  • Notes can be recorded for specific dates.

  • Functions can be started – and the relevant record viewed or processed – through the given events. These events pertain to specific transaction dates (e.g., LC expiry dates).

The availability of events to the end-user is FAP-controlled: the user must have rights to the related function in order to view and access the events.

Figure 11. 1 The Calendar Events Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Calendar Events widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Calendar Events Widget

Parameter Settings

The main parameter settings for the Calendar Events widget are configured in the Widget Maintain function. This includes widget profile and advanced settings.

Additional parameter settings are required: sub-catalogs.

Widget Profile Settings

To configure the profile settings for the Calendar Events widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget. Make sure that the Widget Name is set to: CalendarEvents. Click on the Save button. NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
9. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\CalendarEvents\widget.xml
10. The content of the imported file is shown on the configuration window. Check or modify the settings as required.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
11. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: WIDGET PROFILE Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The CALENDAR_EVENTS.xml and widget.xml files for the new widget profile are generated on the following path: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\ CalendarEvents This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.

Advanced Widget Settings

The advanced settings for the Calendar Events widget involve:

  • Configuring the sub-catalogs to be utilized by this widget

  • Associating the sub-catalogs to the types of events to be used by this widget

Sub-Catalog Settings

The events in the Calendar Events widget are made accessible through the sub-catalogs of the related transaction function.

For each type of event to be utilized by the Calendar Events widget, two sub-catalogs are required:

  • A sub-catalog for searching and displaying records that match a specific date event (e.g., LC maturity date). These records are accessed through the relevant date in the Calendar Events widget.

  • A sub-catalog for searching the number of records for this (date) event

    To create a sub-catalog for an event type:

Do the following . . .
1. Run Transaction Function from the Transaction Function group.
2. Access the module, event, and function for which the sub-catalog is to be defined. EXAMPLE: Module: Import Letters of Credit Event: System Maintenance Function: IMLC View Import LC
3. Access the Catalog component of the function. Two tabs are provided: Main Catalog and Sub Catalog. NOTE: The function must already have a defined main catalog.
4. Access the Sub Catalog tab.
NOTE: If the event requires multiple tables: The Catalog parameter must be manually defined in [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\CalendarEvents\calendar.xml. Specify the multi-table inquiry parameter settings (catalog settings, multiple tables) accordingly. An adapter must be defined for the sub-catalog (through the Adapter flag and dropdown list).
Sub-Catalog for Displaying and Processing the Date Event Records From the Sub Catalog tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar to add a sub-catalog.
Define the sub-catalog details.
Define the criteria for the sub-catalog.
EXAMPLE: Date of IMLC Expiring LCs: This sub-catalog is used for searching LC records that expire on a specific date. EXPIRY_DT: The value is retrieved from the database.
The first Value or FROM_DATE: The value pertains to the first date on the Calendar page that is displayed.
The second Value or TO_DATE: The value pertains to the last date on the Calendar page that is displayed.
Sub-Catalog for the Number of Event Records From the Sub Catalog tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar to add a sub-catalog.
Define the sub-catalog details.
Define the criteria for the sub-catalog.
EXAMPLE: Number of IMLC Expiring LCs: This sub-catalog is used for determining the number of LC records that expire on a specific date. EXPIRY_DT: The value is retrieved from the database.
The first Value or CURR_DATE: The value pertains to the current date on which the transaction is to be performed. The alias name must be set to CURR_DATE. (The value is the same as that of the second Value or CURR_DATE.)
The second Value or CURR_DATE: The value pertains to the current date on which the transaction is to be performed. The alias name must be set to CURR_DATE. (The value is the same as that of the first Value or CURR_DATE.)
Other Sub-Catalogs Add as many sub-catalogs as required. EXAMPLE: Sub-catalogs defined for IMLC View Import LC: Number of IMLC Maturing LCs Date of IMLC Maturing LCs Number of IMLC Expiring LCs Date of IMLC Expiring LCs
XML GENERATION: Run the XML Generator function and generate the relevant XML files.

Event Settings

Once the relevant sub-catalogs have been defined, these must then be associated to the event types of the Calendar Events widget.

These event types are configured as advanced settings in the Widget Maintain function.

Configuration

Associating event types and sub-catalogs is configured through the Event Setting window.

Figure 11. 2 Event Setting Window

Field Field Description
Event
Event Name Specify a unique key for the event. Once the event setting is saved, this event name can no longer be edited.
Event Type Specify the type of event.
Event Title Specify a title for this event type.
NOTE: The actual title shown on the event list of the widget is defined in the related widget.xml file. An example: <iw:item lang=”” id="IMLCExpiringLCs” value="Expiring Import LCs” readOnly="true” alias="elc”> </iw:item>
Module
Module Select the related module from the dropdown list.
Description This displays the description of the selected module.
Functions This displays all the functions of the selected module with defined catalogs. Select the function with the relevant sub-catalog.
Date of Event
Sub Catalog ID This displays the Id of the sub-catalog selected from the Catalog Description dropdown list (for Date of Event).
Catalog Description From the dropdown list, select the sub-catalog to be used for displaying the records for this event. At runtime, the record can be subsequently accessed and processed through this sub-catalog.
Number of Event
Sub Catalog ID This displays the Id of the sub-catalog selected from the Catalog Description dropdown list (for Number of Event).
Catalog Description From the dropdown list, select the sub-catalog to be used for determining the number of records for this event.

Procedure

To configure the event and sub-catalog settings for the Calendar Events widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Access the Advance Setting sub-tab of the main Widget Setting tab (in the Widget Maintain function). Click on the Add button on the toolbar to add an event.
2. The Event Setting window is displayed. Define the event details, and click on the Save button.
3. Selected event details are shown in the grid of the Advance Setting sub-tab.
4. Add as many event types as required. NOTE: The Up and Down buttons can be used to arrange the order of events.
XML GENERATION: ADVANCED WIDGET SETTINGS Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML files are generated on this path: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\CalendarEvents

Browser Settings

Before using the Calendar Events widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Calendar Events to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Calendar Events Widget

To use the Calendar Events widget:

Do the following . . .
Accessing the Calendar Events Widget Click on the relevant tab to access the Calendar Events widget.
The Calendar Events widget window is divided into two sections: The calendar section The events section
NOTE: The Calendar Events widget provides a menu containing the Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the following topic.
Arrow buttons are provided for navigating between months and years.
The days highlighted in red pertain to weekends.
The day selected by default pertains to the present day.
A flag indicates that there are events for the day.
The H marker indicates that the day is a holiday.
The days in gray pertain to days from a different month.
Adding an Event To add an event for a specific date, access the relevant month and year in the calendar section. NOTE: When there are no events or notes defined for a certain date, the events section displays this message: NO EVENTS.
Select the specific day.
Click on the Add icon at the bottom right corner of the widget window. NOTE: The Today button can be used to automatically go back to the current month and year page of the calendar.
The Calendar Events window is displayed.
Specify the event details, and click on the Save button. NOTE: To discard the information and go back to the main widget window, click on the Cancel button.
The system returns to the main Calendar Events window. On the calendar section, the day is marked with a flag. On the events section, a My Note link is added.
To view the notes for a specific date, select the specific date and click on the My Note link.
The Calendar Events window is displayed. The defined notes are shown.
Details can be added or edited as required. Click on the Save button. NOTE: To delete the current details, click on the Remove button.
Accessing the Events of a Day and Processing Transactions There are events for a day when it is marked with a flag. These events pertain to specific dates (e.g., expiring import LCs). In the calendar section, select the relevant date. The types of events for the day are then listed in the events section. For each event type, the number of records is also shown. EXAMPLE: There is one event type for December 22, 2016: Expiring Import LCs. There are twelve events for this event type.
Accessing All the Transactions for an Event Click on the link of the event type.
The system displays the transaction function related to the event type. Specifically, the event records are listed in the transaction function catalog. View or process the relevant transaction accordingly.
Accessing a Specific Transaction for an Event Click on the arrow button that corresponds to the relevant event type. The records for this event type are listed. Click on the specific record to be processed.
The system opens the record in the related transaction function. View or process the transaction accordingly.

Changing the Calendar Events Widget Properties

The properties of the Calendar Events widget can be modified in two ways:

  • The Edit mode of the widget, for customizing how the widget works

  • The Personalize link on the CE landing page, for changing the title and description of the widget

Edit Mode

To customize the functionalities of the Calendar Events widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Open the menu for the Calendar Events widget and click on the Edit option. NOTE: The menu also provides the Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options.
2. The Calendar Events – Edit window is displayed. Select the types of events that are to be made available in the widget. To select all the events, mark the All Events flag. When an event type is relevant to a certain date, the event type is shown and the related records are made accessible. Click on the Save button.
3. The system returns to the main Calendar Events widget window. The event types, when applicable to a certain date, are shown on the events section of the widget window. NOTE: These dates with events are marked with flags.

Title and Description

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Calendar Events widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Calendar Events window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Calendar Events window provides a menu with the Remove, Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the previous topic.
4. Modify the Calendar Events title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Calendar Events widget reflects the new title and description.

The Criteria Search Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings

  • Browser SEttings

Overview

The Criteria Search widget is a tool for defining filter settings to search for specific records. The search process is initiated by way of catalogs. Through these catalogs, records can be subsequently viewed or processed.

The availability of a function to the end-user is FAP-controlled: the user must have rights to the related function in order to run it and access the records.

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Criteria Search widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

3. Select the relevant catalog from the Search For dropdown list.

5. The system lists the resulting records in the catalog page, which corresponds to a specific transaction function. View or process the relevant transaction accordingly.

Changing the Criteria Search Widget Properties

  • The Edit mode of the widget, for customizing how the widget works

  • The Personalize link on the CE landing page, for changing the title and description of the widget

    Edit Mode

    To customize the functionalities of the Criteria Search widget:

3. To add another catalog, select it from the Add Searching Item dropdown list.
4. The catalog is then added to the list. Click on the Save button to save the setting.
NOTE: Every catalog is provided with buttons that are used for: Deleting the catalog from the list; and Changing the position of the catalog on the list.
5. The system returns to the main Criteria Search widget window.
The added function is now included in the Search For dropdown list.

The Dashboard Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings

  • Browser SEttings

Overview

The Dashboard widget is used to access a specific catalog and subsequently view or process a record.

A catalog – inbox, product catalog, or function catalog – generally represents a specific type of transaction. Examples are LC transactions that are awaiting confirmation; Export Collection transactions that are awaiting authorization; and Import Collection transactions that have been rejected.

The availability of a catalog to the end-user is FAP-controlled: the user must have rights to the related function in order to view and access the corresponding records.

EXAMPLE:

The Import Letters of Credit – Awaiting Authorization catalog is included in the dashboard. If –

  • There are 10 records for this catalog.

  • The logged-on user has no access rights (FAP) to the related function.

–The catalog is shown to the user but with no records.

Figure 13. 1 The Dashboard Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Dashboard widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Dashboard Widget

Parameter Settings

The parameter settings for the Dashboard widget are configured in the Widget Maintain function. This includes widget profile and advanced settings.

NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.

7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.

NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension

It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Dashboard\widget.xml

NOTE: The number of rows and columns in the default layout of the dashboard is defined through the boardLayout attribute. The maximum number of rows and columns, on the other hand, is defined through the maxCapacity attribute.

Changing the Dashboard Widget Properties

The properties of the Dashboard widget can be modified in two ways:

  • The Edit mode of the widget, for customizing how the widget works

  • The Personalize link on the CE landing page, for changing the title and description of the widget

Edit Mode

To customize the functionalities of the Dashboard widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Open the menu for the Dashboard widget and click on the Edit option. NOTE: The menu also provides the Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options.
2. The Dashboard – Edit window is displayed. The Row Count and Column Count fields indicate the number of rows and columns to be allotted for the catalogs. The number of dropdown lists corresponds to the indicated number of rows and columns. Each dropdown list, in turn, typically corresponds to a catalog that is currently available in the widget.
NOTE: If no catalog is selected from a dropdown list, a corresponding area is allotted in the actual widget. Compare: The layout of the widget elements on Edit mode: 2 rows 2 columns Instead of 4 catalogs, only 2 are selected.
The layout on the actual widget shows only 2 dropdown lists. The available space, however, indicates that 2 more dropdown lists can be accommodated by the widget.
3. Select the number of rows from the Row Count dropdown list. NOTE: The maximum number of rows that can be selected depends on the setting in the widget configuration file.
4. Select the number of columns from the Column Count dropdown list. NOTE: The maximum number of columns that can be selected depends on the setting in the widget configuration file.
5. Dropdown lists that correspond to the indicated number of rows and columns are automatically displayed.
6. For each dropdown list, select the catalog to be made available in the Dashboard widget.
7. Click on the Save button to save the settings.
8. The system returns to the main Dashboard widget window.
The Dashboard reflects the catalog types in the defined layout. The number of records for each catalog type is indicated in red.

Title and Description

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Dashboard widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Dashboard window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Dashboard window provides a menu with the Remove, Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the previous topic.
4. Modify the Dashboard title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Dashboard widget reflects the new title and description.

The Exchange Rate Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Exchange Rate widget is used for:

  • Determining the current exchange rates of currencies – specifically, in relation to a base currency

  • Calculating the equivalent of an amount in another currency

Figure 14. 1 The Exchange Rate Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Exchange Rate widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Exchange Rate Widget

Parameter Settings

The parameter settings for the Exchange Rate widget are configured in the Widget Maintain function.

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget. Make sure that the Widget Name is set to: ExchangeRate. Click on the Save button. NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
9. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\ExchangeRate\widget.xml
10. The content of the imported file is shown on the configuration window. Check or modify the settings as required.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
The maximum number of currencies that can be displayed by the widget is defined through the maxCount attribute.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
11. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\ExchangeRate\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.

Browser Settings

Before using the Exchange Rate widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Exchange Rate widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine> The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Exchange Rate Widget

To use the Exchange Rate widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Exchange Rate widget.
The Exchange Rate widget consists of two tabs: Exchange Rate and Currency Calculator.
NOTE: The Exchange Rate widget provides a menu containing the Edit, Refresh, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the following topic. The exchange rate data are retrieved from the database. Click on the Refresh window option in order to load the updated values.
Exchange Rate Tab The Exchange Rate tab provides a list of currency exchange rates.
The base currency is listed on the top and highlighted in yellow (e.g., USD). To change the base currency, click on the new currency (e.g., EUR).
The new base currency is shown on the top and highlighted in yellow.
Currency Calculator Tab The Currency Calculator tab is used to calculate the equivalent of an amount in another currency.
Use the Currency I Have and Currency I Want fields to calculate currency conversions and equivalents. NOTE: To reset the values, click on the Clear button.

Changing the Exchange Rate Widget Properties

The properties of the Exchange Rate widget can be modified in two ways:

  • The Edit mode of the widget, for customizing how the widget works

  • The Personalize link on the CE landing page, for changing the title and description of the widget

    Edit Mode

    To customize the functionalities of the Exchange Rate widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Open the menu for the Exchange Rate widget and click on the Edit option. NOTE: The menu also provides the Refresh, Minimize, and Help window options.
2. The Exchange Rate – Edit window is displayed.
3. To change the base currency, select the new currency from the Set Base Currency dropdown list.
To save the last selected currency as the base currency (set either thru the Edit mode or through the main widget window), mark the Remember Last Base Currency flag. NOTE: If this flag is not marked, and another base currency is selected in the main widget window, the system displays the last saved base currency when the widget is refreshed or reloaded – and not the most recent currency selected as the base currency in the main widget window.
4. To add a currency to the currency list of the widget, select the relevant currency from the Add Currency dropdown list. The added currency is now included in the currency list. NOTE: The maximum number of currencies to be displayed on the widget depends on the setting in the widget configuration file.
Every currency is provided with buttons that are used for: Deleting the currency from the list; and Changing the position of the currency on the list.
5. Click on the Save button to save the settings.
6. The system returns to the main Exchange Rate widget window, which now reflects the defined settings.

Title and Description

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Exchange Rate widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Exchange Rate window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Exchange Rate window provides a menu with the Remove, Edit, Refresh, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the previous topic.
4. Modify the Exchange Rate title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Exchange Rate widget reflects the new title and description.

The Main Menu Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings

  • Browser Settings

  • Special Features

Overview

The Main Menu widget provides the list of CE products and the corresponding functions. This is the common way by which functions are run and related transactions are processed.

The availability of products and functions to the end-user is FAP-controlled.

Figure 15. 1 The Main Menu Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Main Menu widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Main Menu Widget

Parameter Settings

The parameter settings for the Main Menu widget are configured in the Widget Maintain function.

Do the following . . .

7. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
8. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\MainMenu\widget.xml

Using the Main Menu Widget

To use the Main Menu widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Main Menu widget.
2. A transaction can be processed through the Main Menu widget in two ways: By directly running the transaction function By searching for the transaction function
NOTE: The Main Menu widget provides a menu containing the Refresh, Minimize, Maximize, and Help window options.
Running the Transaction Function Directly Click on the relevant product (e.g., Import Letters of Credit).
The list of functions for the product is displayed.
Run the relevant function (e.g., Apply for Import LC).
NOTE: The leftmost arrow button – Back to Product – can be used to go back to the list of products. The rightmost arrow buttons – Previous and Next – are used for navigating between products.
The transaction function screen or catalog is displayed. View or process the transaction accordingly.
Using the Search For Option Specify a keyword and click on the relevant function from the search results (e.g., Authorise Transaction function for the Import Letters of Credit product).
The transaction function screen or catalog is displayed. View or process the transaction accordingly.

Changing the Main Menu Widget Properties

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Main Menu widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Special Features

Expandable and Collapsible Menu

The default way of opening and closing a product’s function list in the Main Menu widget is this:

  • Click on the product name to display the functions.

  • Click on the bottom left arrow button to close the function list.

    An alternative way, in which the product name can be clicked to close the function list, can be set up. This involves modifying specific codes in the following file:

    CEWeb.war\widgets\framework\plugins\Plugins.js

    For details on the required modification, refer to the related material that accompanies the CE Version 3.3.0 release.

EXAMPLE
1. With the Main Menu widget configured to work in the aforementioned alternative way, access the CE landing page.
2. Click on a product name.
3. The product menu is expanded to display the functions.
4. To collapse the menu, click on the product name again.
NOTE: With the default Main Menu widget setting, the function menu is closed by clicking on the bottom left arrow. This method still works if the Main Menu is set up to work in the alternative way.
5. The product menu is closed.

The Notice Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Notice widget is used for viewing the notification messages sent to the current (logged-on) user.

These messages may serve to:

  • Inform the user of a completed transaction or process (e.g., a completed LC transaction)

  • Notify a user of a pending process or action (e.g., an LC transaction that requires authorization)

  • Alert the user of a transaction result or status (e.g., an LC transaction that has been rejected)

In addition, these notifications serve as links for continuing the transaction process.

Figure 16. 1 The Notice Widget

NOTE:

  1. For a quick overview on how the Notice widget works, refer to Chapter 16: Browser Settings > Using the Notice Widget.

  2. Refer to the CE Supplementary Functions document for more information on generating widget notices.

Parameter Settings

The main parameter settings for the Notice widget are configured in the Widget Maintain and Output Device functions. Other parameters are those for the Notice and Label browser functions. Depending on the type of notifications to be defined, other parameters may be required as well.

Widget Parameters

To configure the main Notice widget parameters:

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget. Make sure that the Widget Name is set to: Notification. Click on the Save button. NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
9. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Notification\widget.xml
10. The content of the imported file is shown on the configuration window. Check or modify the settings as required.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
NOTE: The default number of notifications to be shown on the widget is defined through the listSize attribute.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
11. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\ Notification\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.
NOTE: The options for the number of notifications to be shown on the widget are defined through the panelRecords attributes in this file: CE.ear\CEWeb.war\widgets\Notification\notification.css

Other Parameters

The Notice widget functions in combination with these products: Notice View and Label. In addition, templates for the actual notifications are also required.

NOTE:

  1. Depending on the transaction or notification requirements, other parameter settings may be required. Examples of which are authorization rules and user classes; these typically dictate the flow of notification messages.

  2. For additional details on the View Notice Detail function and the Label functions, refer to the CE Standing Data Functions documentation.

View Notice Detail Function

Do the following . . .
(The View Notice detail function as shown on the browser)
Transaction Function settings: Module: Standing Module (STAN) Event: Notification Maintain Transaction function: View Notice Detail
Product settings: Product Group: Customer Standing Data Product: Notification Product Function: View Notice Detail

Label Functions

Do the following . . .
(The Label functions as shown on the browser)
Transaction Function settings: Module: Standing Module (STAN) Event: Notification Maintain Transaction functions: Add Notification Label Edit Notification Label View Notification Label Delete Notification Label Unlock Notification Label
Product settings: Product Group: Customer Standing Data Product: Label Product Functions: Add Notification Label Edit Notification Label View Notification Label Delete Notification Label Unlock Notification Label

Notification Templates

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Output Device function from the System Function group.
2. The Output Device function window is displayed. Click on the Mail/Fax/Notice/SMS tab.
3. Click on the Notice sub-tab.
Select the Template node, and click on the Add button on the toolbar.
4. The Event Setting window is displayed.
5. Specify the name and description of the template in the Template Name and Template Subject fields, respectively.
6. Using the button that accompanies the Template Content field, browse for the template file to be used for the actual notification (content).
NOTE: These template files must be stored in, and retrieved from, this directory: [CE Parameter Drive]\[CE_SYS]\FTL\MAIL
7. Select the functionality of this specific template from the Notification Type dropdown list: Message: Select this option if the template is used to display a simple notification or message.
Task: Select this option if the template is used: to display a simple notification or message; and allow the end-user to continue the transaction process through a function. From the function list, select the function to be associated with this template.
8. Click on the Save button to save the settings.
XML GENERATION: WIDGET PROFILE Run the XML Generator function and select the Notification parameter type. Make sure to mark the created template in the XML Generator – Notification at is displayed.
The XML file for the new notification template is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\[Bank Group]\[Country]\AP\NOTIFICATION\NOTIFICATION_TEMPLATE.XML This file contains the details of all created notification templates.

Notification Settings for Transaction Functions

Do the following . . .
Certain transaction functions generate notification messages. To define the settings for these messages, run Transaction Function. Access the relevant module, event, and function. EXAMPLE: Module: Import Letters of Credit Event: Transaction Function
Access the Notify function component and define the Notification settings.
EXAMPLE 1: Notification settings for the Apply for Import LC function.
EXAMPLE 2: Notification settings for the IMLC Authorise Transaction function.

Browser Settings

Before using the Notification widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Notification widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Notice Widget

To use the Notice widget:

Do the following . . .
Accessing the Notice Widget Click on the relevant tab to access the Notice widget.
The Notice widget provides: Buttons and options: Labels, Filter, More, Trash The total number of notifications Links for directly accessing a transaction or notification Open More link, for displaying more transaction records
NOTE: The Notice widget provides a menu containing the Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the following topic.
Handling a Notification To view or process a transaction directly, click on the appropriate notification.
The Task Detail page is displayed. Basic information on the transaction or notification is provided. To continue processing the transaction, click on the Process button.
The relevant transaction function is displayed. Process the transaction accordingly. NOTE: Notifications can also be viewed and subsequently processed through the View Notification Detail function of the Notification View product.
Displaying All Notifications To display all the notifications, click on the Open More link on the bottom right corner of the window. NOTE: The total number of notifications is indicated on the upper right corner of the window.
A page is displayed listing all the notifications.
The Read Status dropdown list can be used for filtering the types of notifications to be displayed: All, Read, or Unread. Select the relevant option and click on the Filter option. Pagination options are also provided for navigating between pages of notifications. To view or process a transaction, click on the notification link. Refer to the preceding Handling a Notification section. NOTE: To display all the records again – read and unread – click on the Reset option.
Labeling a Notification Mark the specific notification and click on the Labels button. A list of available labels is displayed; select the relevant label. NOTE: Labels are maintained in the Label product.
The specific notification is now designated with the selected label. NOTE: To remove the label of a notification: Select the notification; and Open the Labels dropdown list and select the same label.
Filtering Notifications To display only specific notifications, click on the Filter button. Select the type from the list that is displayed: All, Read, or Unread. NOTE: Notifications may be further filtered based on its read status and date. Refer to the succeeding Filtering Notifications discussion in this chapter for more details.
Marking Notifications as Read or Unread Mark the specific notification and click on the More button. Select the relevant option from the list that is displayed: Mark as Read or Mark as Unread. NOTE: Unread notifications are highlighted in gray.
Deleting Notifications To delete a notification, select it and click on the Trash icon.
Filtering Notifications Notifications in the Notice widget may be filtered based on their read status and the date on which the notification has been received. To do this, the catalog setting of the View Notice Details function must first be modified. Configuration Modify the View Notice Detail function catalog condition as: Generate the XML file for the function catalog. Modify the following files. Transaction Processing

  1. Log on to the CE Utility. In the Notice widget, click on the Open More link.

  2. All available notification records are listed. Additional filter option fields are shown. Specify the Read Status and From and To dates. Click on the Filter link.

  3. The relevant notification records are shown based on the defined filter criteria. Click on the Reset link.

  4. All defined filter criteria are removed and all the notification records are shown.
