The Quick Access Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter SEttings

  • Browser SEttings

Overview

The Quick Access function is used for directly accessing frequently run functions.

The availability of a function to the end-user is FAP-controlled: the user must have the relevant function access rights.

Figure 17. 1 The Quick Access Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Quick Access widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Quick Access Widget

Parameter Settings

The parameter settings for the Quick Access widget are configured in the Widget Maintain function. This includes widget profile and advanced settings.

Widget Profile Settings

To configure the profile settings for the Quick Access widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget. Make sure that the Widget Name is set to: QuickAccess. Click on the Save button. NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
9. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\QuickAccess\widget.xml
10. The content of the imported file is shown on the configuration window. Check or modify the settings as required.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
The default number of functions to be shown on the widget is defined through the listCount attribute.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
11. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: WIDGET PROFILE Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\QuickAccess\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.
NOTE: The options for the number of functions to be shown on the widget are defined through the options attributes in this file: CE.ear\CEWeb.war\widgets\QuickAccess\quickaccess.js

Advanced Widget Settings

The advanced settings for the Quick Access widget involve selecting the specific functions to be utilized by the widget.

Configuration

These advanced Quick Access widget settings are configured through the Event Setting – Quick Access List window.

Figure 17. 2 Event Setting – Quick Access List Window

Field Field Description
Quick Access List
Product Catalog List This section lists the available product groups, products, and functions. Open the product group and product, and select the relevant function. Click on the Add button to include it as one of the functions to be utilized by the Quick Access widget. The selected function is also added to the Function List. To add all the functions from a product, select the product and click on the >> button. The functions under this product are added to the Function List.
(Function List) This section lists the Id, name, description, and path (product) of the selected functions. NOTE: Use the Clear and Clear All buttons to remove functions from the list.

Procedure

To configure the advanced settings of the Quick Access widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Access the Advance Setting sub-tab of the main Widget Setting tab (in the Widget Maintain function). Click on the Add button on the toolbar to add an event.
2. The Event Setting – Quick Access List window is displayed. Select the relevant functions to be utilized by the Quick Access widget.
Click on the Save button when done.
3. Selected function details are shown in the grid of the Advance Setting sub-tab. Add as many functions as required.
XML GENERATION: ADVANCED WIDGET SETTINGS Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML files are generated on this path: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\QuickAccess

Browser Settings

Before using the Quick Access widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Quick Access widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Quick Access Widget

To use the Quick Access widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Quick Access widget.
2. The Quick Access widget lists the functions that are made available to this widget.
NOTE: The Quick Access widget provides a menu containing the Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the following topic.
3. Click on the relevant link to directly access a function.
4. The function screen is displayed. Create or process a transaction accordingly.

Changing the Quick Access Widget Properties

The properties of the Quick Access widget can be modified in two ways:

  • The Edit mode of the widget, for customizing how the widget works

  • The Personalize link on the CE landing page, for changing the title and description of the widget

    Edit Mode

    To customize the functionalities of the Quick Access widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Open the menu for the Quick Access widget and click on the Edit option. NOTE: The menu also provides the Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options.
2. The Quick Access – Edit window is displayed.
3. To change the number of functions that can be shown on the Quick Access widget, select the number from The Total Count dropdown list. NOTE: The maximum number of functions that can be displayed on the widget depends on the setting in the widget configuration file.
4. To add a function to be displayed on the Quick Access widget, select it from the Select to Add dropdown list. The function is automatically added in the function list.
Up to the indicated number of functions can be added to the list.
NOTE: Every function is provided with buttons that are used for: Deleting the function from the list; and Changing the position of the function on the list.
5. Click on the Save button to save the settings.
6. The system returns to the main Quick Access widget window. The widget reflects the selected functions, the number of which complies with the defined number of functions to be displayed.

Title and Description

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Quick Access widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Quick Access window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Quick Access window provides a menu with the Remove, Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the previous topic.
4. Modify the Quick Access title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Quick Access widget reflects the new title and description.

The Recent Functions Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Recent Functions widget is used for directly accessing the functions that have been recently run by the logged-on user.

The availability of the functions to the end-user is FAP-controlled.

Figure 18. 1 The Recent Functions Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Recent Functions widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Recent Functions Widget

Parameter Settings

The parameter settings for the Recent Functions widget are configured in the Widget Maintain function.

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget. Make sure that the Widget Name is set to: RecentFunction. Click on the Save button. NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
9. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\RecentFunction\widget.xml
10. The content of the imported file is shown on the configuration window. Check or modify the settings as required.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
NOTE: The default number of recent functions to be shown on the widget is defined through the listCount attribute.
11. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\RecentFunction\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.
NOTE: The options for the number of recent functions to be shown on the widget are defined through the options attributes in this file: CE.ear\CEWeb.war\widgets\RecentFunction\ recentfunc.js

Browser Settings

Before using the Recent Functions widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Recent Widget widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Recent Functions Widget

To use the Recent Functions widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Recent Functions widget.
2. The Recent Functions widget lists all the functions that have been recently run by the logged-on user. NOTE: The system generates the function list according to the user access log.
NOTE: The Recent Functions widget provides a menu containing the Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the following topic.
3. Click on the relevant link to directly access a function.
4. The function screen is displayed. Create or process a transaction accordingly.

Changing the Recent Functions Widget Properties

The properties of the Recent Functions widget can be modified in two ways:

  • The Edit mode of the widget, for customizing how the widget works

  • The Personalize link on the CE landing page, for changing the title and description of the widget

    Edit Mode

    To customize the functionalities of the Recent Functions widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Open the menu for the Recent Functions widget and click on the Edit option. NOTE: The menu also provides the Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options.
2. The Recent Functions – Edit window is displayed. The product name can be hidden or shown alongside the function name in the widget. Mark or unmark the Show Product Description Before the Function flag accordingly.
3. Define the limit for the number of recent functions to be shown on the widget: select the number from the Total Record Count dropdown list. NOTE: The default number of functions shown is five.
4. Click on the Save button to save the settings.
5. The system returns to the main Recent Functions widget window which now reflects the defined settings.

Title and Description

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Recent Functions widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Recent Functions window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Recent Functions window provides a menu with the Remove, Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the previous topic.
4. Modify the Recent Functions title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Recent Functions widget reflects the new title and description.

The Summary Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter SEttings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Summary widget is used for viewing the summary details of transactions through a specific type of catalog: inbox catalog, function catalog, or product catalog. In addition, the transaction can be directly accessed and subsequently processed.

The availability of a Summary widget to the end-user is FAP-controlled: the user must have rights to the specific function utilized by the widget.

Figure 19. 1 The Summary Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Summary widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Summary Widget

Parameter Settings

The parameter settings for the Summary widget are configured in the Widget Maintain function. This includes widget profile and advanced settings.

NOTE: The Summary widget is used for viewing and accessing one type of records only (via catalog). The widget must be configured on Edit mode in order to display records from other particular catalogs.

For easier and faster access to the records of other catalogs, additional Summary widgets can be created – these have the same primary attributes as the standard Summary widgets. Refer to this discussion for an example:

Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension

Widget Profile Settings

To configure the profile settings for the Summary widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget. Make sure that the Widget Name is set to: Summary. Click on the Save button. NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
9. The Open dialog box is displayed. Browse for the widget.xml file – i.e., the widget definition file –from the relevant directory. NOTE: The widget.xml can be placed in any directory. It can also be modified directly and later imported through this same process. EXAMPLE: AppSrv01\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Summary\widget.xml
10. The content of the imported file is shown on the configuration window. Check or modify the settings as required.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
NOTE: The default number of records to be shown on the widget is defined through the listCount attribute.
11. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: WIDGET PROFILE Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Summary\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.
NOTE: The options for the number of records to be shown on the widget are defined through the options attributes in this file: CE.ear\CEWeb.war\widgets\Summary\summary.js

Advanced Widget Settings

The advanced settings for the Summary widget involve selecting the specific catalogs to be utilized by the widget.

Configuration

These advanced Summary widget settings are configured through the Event Setting – Summary List window.

Figure 19. 2 Event Setting – Summary List Window

Field Field Description
Summary List
Item Description Specify the title to be used by the widget in displaying the summary data of a particular catalog.
EXAMPLE: Parameter setting – Item Description
Browser – Summary widget title
Catalog Type Select from the dropdown list the type of catalog to be utilized by the Summary widget. Inbox Catalog Function Catalog Product Catalog NOTE: The Event Setting – Summary List window is altered according to the selected catalog type. Specifically, the Catalog List section is changed. Refer to the following Catalog List section.
(Catalog List) Depending on the catalog type selected, this section displays one of the following types of lists:
Title/Item, for the Inbox Catalog type. Statistics catalogs are shown. (Statistics catalogs are defined through the Inbox function.)
Function Catalog, for the Function Catalog type. The modules, events, and transaction functions are shown. (Function catalogs are defined through Transaction Function.)
Products Catalog, for the Product Catalog type. The product groups, products, and functions are shown. (Product catalogs are defined through the Product Catalog function.)
Click on the specific catalog. The fields for the selected catalog are added to the Field List section.
(Field List) This section lists the fields from the selected catalog. These are the fields to be displayed on the Summary list.
NOTE: The field list includes all the fields from the selected (source) catalog that are not hidden. To hide a field from the Summary widget, mark the corresponding Hidden flag. Fields in the Event Setting – Summary List window: Fields from the source catalog:

Procedure

To configure the advanced settings of the Summary widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Access the Advance Setting sub-tab of the main Widget Setting tab (in the Widget Maintain function). Click on the Add button on the toolbar to add an event.
2. The Event Setting – Summary List window is displayed. Define the catalog details, and click on the Save button.
3. The defined Item Description and Catalog Type are shown in the grid of the Advance Setting sub-tab.
4. Add as many catalogs as required. NOTE: The Up and Down buttons can be used to arrange the order of catalogs.
NOTE: On the CE browser, the records of only one catalog can be shown on the Summary widget. Displaying the records of another catalog is done through Edit mode. For details, refer to the next topic: Browser Settings
NOTE: Another Summary widget can be created based on the settings of the native Summary widget. (For details, refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
XML GENERATION: ADVANCED WIDGET SETTINGS Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML files are generated on this path: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Summary

Browser Settings

Before using the Summary widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Summary widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Summary Widget

To use the Summary widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Summary widget.
2. The Summary widget lists the summary details of the transactions for a specific catalog (e.g., View Import LC). The number of records is also shown.
NOTE: The Summary widget provides a menu containing the Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the following topic.
3. To view all the transactions, click on the Open More link.
4. The system displays the records in the catalog page that, in turn, corresponds to a specific transaction function. View or process the relevant transaction accordingly.

Changing the Summary Widget Properties

The properties of the Summary widget can be modified in two ways:

  • The Edit mode of the widget, for customizing how the widget works

  • The Personalize link on the CE landing page, for changing the title and description of the widget

    Edit Mode

    To customize the functionalities of the Summary widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Open the menu for the Summary widget and click on the Edit option. NOTE: The menu also provides the Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options.
2. The Summary – Edit window is displayed.
3. To change the type of records to be displayed by the Summary widget, open the Function List dropdown list and select the relevant catalog.
4. To change the maximum number of records to be displayed on the Summary widget, select the relevant number from the Record Count dropdown list.
5. Click on the Save button to save the settings.
6. The system returns to the main Summary widget window. The widget now reflects the defined settings.

Title and Description

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Summary widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Summary window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Summary window provides a menu with the Remove, Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the previous topic.
4. Modify the Summary title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Summary widget reflects the new title and description.

The Upload Message Widget

  • Overview

  • parameter Settings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Upload Message widget is used for directly uploading a file for the Purchase Order product, without having to go through the Upload Purchase Order function.

If the user does not have access rights (FAP) to the Purchase Order product and Upload Purchase Order function, the Upload Message widget is still shown. Attempts to upload any file, however, are not allowed by the system.

Figure 20. 1 The Upload Message Widget

NOTE: For a quick overview on how the Upload Message widget works, refer to the following discussion in this chapter:

Browser Settings > Using the Upload Message Widget

NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings

5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. To import predefined settings for the widget profile, click on the browse button for the Import Definition File option. NOTE: The Extend Definition File option is used for applying the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension

Browser Settings

Before using the Upload Message widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Upload Message widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

NOTE: If the user does not have access rights (FAP) to functions with upload feature (e.g., Upload Invoice and Upload Purchase Order(s) functions), the Upload Message widget is still shown. Attempts to upload any file, however, are not allowed by the system.

Using the Upload Message Widget

To use the Upload Message widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Upload Message widget.
2. The Upload Message widget provides: File field Browse button Upload button
NOTE: The Upload Message widget also provides a menu containing the Refresh, Minimize, and Help window options.
3. To upload a file, click on the Browse button.
4. In the dialog box that is displayed, browse for and select the relevant file. Click on the Open button. NOTE: The types of files that can be uploaded depend on what is allowed by the specific function (e.g., ZIP and XML for Upload Purchase Order(s) function).
5. In the Upload Message widget, click on the Upload button to proceed with uploading the file.

Changing the Upload Message Widget Properties

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Upload Message widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Upload Message window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Upload Message window provides a menu with the Remove, Refresh, Minimize, and Help window options.
4. Modify the Upload Message title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Upload Message widget reflects the new title and description.

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Welcome widget displays the following details:

  • Welcome message

The username is provided with a link that, when clicked, opens a window for changing the password of the current user.

XML GENERATION: Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\WelcomeBox\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.

Browser Settings

Before using the Welcome widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Welcome widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Welcome Widget

To use the Welcome widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Welcome widget.
2. The Welcome widget displays the following details: The name of the current system user The last successful logon date and time The last failed logon date and time The current logon date and time
3. To change the password, click on the link for the current user.
4. Define the password details in the window that is displayed.

Changing the Welcome Widget Properties

The properties of the Welcome widget can be modified in two ways:

  • The Edit mode of the widget, for customizing how the widget works

  • The Personalize link on the CE landing page, for changing the title and description of the widget

    Edit Mode

    To customize the functionalities of the Welcome widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Open the menu for the Welcome widget and click on the Edit option. NOTE: The menu also provides the Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options.
2. The Welcome – Edit window is displayed. The original Welcome message is shown in the field provided. NOTE: The original Welcome message is: “Logon date and time:".
3. Modify the Welcome message as required, and click on the Save button.
4. The system returns to the main Welcome widget window.
The new Welcome message is now displayed.

Title and Description

Through the Personalize link, the title and description of the Welcome widget can be modified. The title appears on the title bar of the widget window. The description, on the other hand, appears as a tooltip.

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the Personalize link.
2. The Personalize page is displayed.
3. The Welcome window shows the current title and description of the widget.
NOTE: The Welcome window provides a menu with the Remove, Edit, Refresh, Maximize, Minimize, and Help window options. The Edit option is discussed in the previous topic.
4. Modify the Welcome title and description, and save the settings.
5. Click on the Save Changes button. NOTE: The Save and Discard links can be used to save and discard changes or actions made.
6. A confirmation message is displayed. Click on the Done button.
7. The system returns to the landing page.
The Welcome widget reflects the new title and description.

The Statistics Widget

  • Overview

  • Parameter Settings for viewData Widget Type

  • Parameter Settings for jumpFunction Widget Type

  • Widget Graphic Settings

  • Browser Settings

Overview

The Statistics widget is used to display transaction statistics using graphical representations such as a line, bar, or a pie chart.

It can be configured for two purposes:

  • Displaying transaction statistics based on criteria defined through an SQL query. The statistics to be displayed on the widget is the result of the query. This is known as the viewData widget type.

  • Displaying statistics of a specific function. In this configuration, the Statistics widget can be clicked, and redirects the user to the related function. This is known as the jumpFunction widget type.

The availability of the statistics to the end-user is may be FAP-controlled: the user must have rights to the related function in order to view and access the corresponding records.

The parameters for the Statistics widget are configured through the following:

  • widget.xml file

  • statistics.xml file

  • Widget Profile settings (for jumpFunction widget type)

Parameter Settings for viewData Widget Type

Widget.xml File

The widget.xml file is used to define whether the Statistics widget is for viewing only or if it is to provide the user the option to directly access a related function after viewing information from the widget.

This file is located in the [Parameter Drive]:\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Statistics folder.

If it is to be used for viewing only, the value of the widgetType parameter must be set to viewData.

Otherwise, the value must be set to jumpFunction.

NOTE: After modifying the widget.xml file, the application server must be restarted.

Figure 22. 1 Statistics Widget: Widget.xml File

Statistics.xml File

The statistics.xml file is used to define the criteria for the information to be displayed in the Statistics widget.

It contains the following elements:

Concept Description
<level1> This element is the main container where the settings for the widget are defined.
<sqlList> This element is where the query or queries are specfied. It has two attributes: NeedFAPCheck: This is used to define whether or not the query requires Function Assignment Permission (FAP) check. Its value can be either of the following: T – If this option is specified, the system adds conditions to the query to conduct an FAP check. If the current user does not have the required FAP for the module specified in the query, the query results for the module are not shown on the widget. F – If this option is specified, the system executes the defined query directly. MultiTable: This is used to define whether or not the query is to be executed for multiple tables in the database. Its value can be either of the following: T – If this option is specified, the query involves multiple tables. The alias of the main table must be set to A. If the value of NeedFAPCheck is T, the system only supports a Master, Event Master, or TRX_INBOX table to be the main table. F – If this option is specified, the query is for a single database table only.
<sql> Inside the <sqlList> element, there can be several <sql> elements. Each <sql> element defines a set of queries. It has two attributes: seriesName – This is used to define the legend name for the data group. If its value is not defined, the system sets it using the format [chart name][chart number]. When the legend name is clicked, the curve for the related data group can be hidden or shown. dsTyp – This is used to define the data source where the query retrieves the data. The data source options are the following: T – This option refers to the transaction data source. It is the default value. A – This option refers to an archiving data source. B – This option refers to a backup data source. The system provides placeholders for the uncertain values in the query. Data Source: $DS is used for the transaction schema. (e.g. $DS.TRX_INBOX) Field Value: the following placeholders are provided for the fields’ value in query condition. The system sets the exact value according to currently logged on user. NOTE: Setting the security schema or tablespace (e.g. CEUSER) as a data source for a query is not supported.
<xAxis> This element is used to define the description for the query result on the X-axis (for bar or line charts). Inside it, there can be several <desc> elements to define the description in different languages. The default description is defined using the <desc lang=”"> element. If two results have the same description, the results are separated by a comma. If the description is not defined, the system uses the query result directly as the description. Example: <xAxis> <desc lang=”"> <![CDATA[P,T:Awaiting Authorization; A,S:Authorised; R:Rejected;]]> </desc> <desc lang="CNS”><![CDATA[P,T:待授权; A,S:已授权; R:拒绝]]> </desc> </xAxis> NOTE: A colon (:) or semicolon (;) is not allowed in the description.
<series> This element is used to define the description for the seriesName legend name in the <sql> element. Inside it, there can be several <desc> elements to define the description in different languages. The default description is defined using the <desc lang=”">. If the description is not defined, the system uses the seriesName value in <sql> element directly. Example: <series> <desc lang=”"> <![CDATA[IMLC:Import LC;OWGT:Guarantees;]]> </desc> <desc lang="CNS”> <![CDATA[IMLC:进口信用证;OWGT:担保;]]> </desc> </series> NOTE: A colon (:) or semicolon (;) is not allowed in the description.

Configuration

Do the following . . .
1. Open the relevant widget.xml file. This file is located in the [Parameter Drive]:\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Statistics folder.
2. Set the value of the widgetType parameter to viewData. Once done, save the changes.
3. Open the statistics.xml file. This file is located in the [Parameter Drive]:\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Statistics folder.
4. Provide the values for the following parameters: <sqlList NeedFAPCheck> <sqlList MultiTable> <sql seriesName> <sql dsType> <xAxis><desc lang> <series><desc lang> Once done, save the changes. NOTE: Refer to Chapter 22: Statistics.xml File for more information on the parameters in the statistics.xml file.
EXAMPLE: Multiple Queries for One Data Set In this example, there are two sets of data; IMLC and OWGT. For each data set, there are three queries: Awaiting Authorization Authorised Rejected The queries for the data set must match the descriptions defined in the X-axis in order for the system to correctly map the query result to its corresponding description.
EXAMPLE: Single Query for One Data Set In this example, only the IMLC data set is defined, and only a single query, LC_CCY information, is specified for the data set. No description is provided for the X-axis parameter; therefore, the system uses the query result directly as the descriptions for the X-axis.
EXAMPLE: Multiple Table Query In this example, specified SQL statement executes the query to multiple tables in the database. When querying to multiple tables, the value of the MultiTable attribute must be set to T and the alias of the main table must be set to A. If the FAP check is required, the system adds conditions based on the main table’s alias (e.g. A.C_UNIT_CODE)
EXAMPLE: Legend Names To define the legend name for a data group, two methods can be used: seriesName – This is used to define the legend name for the data group. If its value is not defined, the system sets it using the format [chart name][chart number]. This element is used to define the description for the seriesName legend name in the <sql> element. Inside it, there can be several <desc> elements to define the description in different languages. The default description is defined using the <desc lang=”">. If the description is not defined, the system uses the seriesName value in <sql> element directly.
EXAMPLE: Multi-language Configuration To enable the multi-language feature for the widget, specify the langage code in the <desc lang> attribute of the <xAxis> and <series> elements. The system checks on the languages defined in the <desc lang> attributes. If the current system language matches a language defined in the <desc lang> attribute, the relevant language is displayed in the Statistics widget.

Parameter Settings for jumpFunction Widget Type

jumpFunction.xml File

The jumpFunction.xml file is used to define the functions to which the user is to be redirected when the Statistics widget is clicked.

It contains the following elements:

Concept Description
<level1> This element is the main container where the settings for the widget are defined. It contains three sub-elements: <functionGroup>, <xAxis> and <fieldInfo>.
<functionGroup> This element is where the related functions are defined. It contains the <functionID> element
<functionID> This element is where a group of related transaction function IDs are specified. The IDs are separated by comma. It contains an attribute: seriesName – This is used to define the legend name for the data group. If its value is not defined, the system sets it using the format [chart name][chart number]. When the legend name is clicked, the curve for the related data group can be hidden or shown. NOTE: Only functions with a catalog are supported in the jumpFunction type of the Statistics widget.
<xAxis> This element is used to define the description for the function on the X-axis (for bar or line charts). Inside it, there can be several <desc> elements to define the description in different languages. The default description is defined using the <desc lang=”"> element. If the description is not defined, the transaction function as the description. The value must be set up if functions in the <functionID> group have thesame description (e.g., function IMLC Authorize and EXLC Authorize have the same function description. In this case the value “Authorise Transaction” must be set up). Example: <xAxis> <desc lang=”"><![CDATA[IMLC;EXLC;IMCO;EXCO;IWGT;OWGT]]> </desc> <desc lang="CNS”><![CDATA[进口信用证;出口信用证;进口托收;出口托收;进口担保;出口担保]]> </desc> </xAxis> NOTE: A colon (:) or semicolon (;) is not allowed in the description.
<series> This element is used to define the description for the seriesName legend name in the <functionID> element. Inside it, there can be several <desc> elements to define the description in different languages. The default description is defined using the <desc lang=”">. If the description is not defined, the system uses the seriesName value in <functionID> element directly. Example: <series> <desc lang=”"> <![CDATA[AUTH:Authorise Transaction;]]></desc> <desc lang="CNS”><![CDATA[AUTH:授权;]]></desc> </series> NOTE: A colon (:) or semicolon (;) is not allowed in the description.

Configuration

Do the following . . .
1. Run the Widget Maintain function from the Transaction Function group.
2. The Widget Maintain window is displayed. The window shows the following tabs: Widget Profile Widget Setting From the Widget Profile tab, click on the Add button on the toolbar.
3. The Widget Profile window is displayed. Specify the required details for the new widget. Make sure that the Widget Name is set to: StatisticsFunc. Click on the Save button. NOTE: For details on the other profile settings, refer to: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Profile Settings
4. The newly created widget profile is displayed in the grid.
5. Click on the Synchronize to DB button in order to update the database with the newly defined widget settings.
6. Access the Widget Setting tab. This contains two sub-tabs: Generate Setting and Advance Setting.
7. From the Frame Work list in the Generate Setting tab, double-click on the newly created widget. Alternatively, select the widget and click on the Edit button on the toolbar.
8. A configuration window is displayed. Select the Extend Definition File option to apply the settings of an existing widget profile to create a new widget profile. From the corresponding dropdown menu, select the relevant definition file. NOTE: Refer to this discussion: Chapter Nine > General Widget Parameter Settings > Widget Definition File Extension
9. The content of the selected file is shown on the configuration window. The value of the widgetType parameter must be set to jumpFunction.
NOTE: To define whether or not multiple instances of the widget can be added to the same tab on the CE browser, set the allowInstanceContent attribute to either: false: Only one instance of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab. true: Multiple instances of the widget can be dragged and dropped to the same tab.
When done with the settings, click on the Save button and close the window.
10. The system returns to the function window, which now shows the content of the imported definition file.
XML GENERATION: Run the XML Generator function and select the Widget Maintain parameter type. Make sure to mark the created widget profile in the XML Generator – Widget Maintain window that is displayed.
The XML file for the new widget profile is generated: [PARAMETER DRIVE]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\StatisticsFunc\widget.xml This is the updated version of the definition file that has been used for the widget profile: widget.xml. The settings only apply to this specific widget profile.
11. Create and configure a new parameter manually in the widget folder [Parameter Drive]:\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\[widget name]\jumpFunction.xml to define the transaction functions to which the user is to be redirected. NOTE: Refer to Chapter Twenty-two: jumpFunction.xml for a detailed discussion on the jumpFunction.xml file.

Widget Graphic Settings

Different types of graphical representations can be used to display information on the Statistics widget. The following types of charts are provided:

  • line graph

  • bar graph

  • pie chart

The system also provides an option to display the details in tabular format below the chart.

These features are configured through the widget.xml file that is located in the [Parameter Drive]: \CE_SYS\WIDGETS\Statistics folder.

NOTE: After modifying the widget.xml file, the application server must be restarted.

Do the following . . .
1. Open the relevant widget.xml file.
2. To display the details using a line graph, set the value of the graphType parameter to line. Once done, save the changes.
EXAMPLE: When the Statistics widget is accessed in the browser, information is illustrated through a line graph.
3. To display the details using a bar graph, set the value of the graphType parameter to bar. To display the vertical bars, set the value of the isLie attribute to F. Otherwise, set its value to T to display horizontal bars. Once done, save the changes.
EXAMPLE: When the Statistics widget is accessed in the browser, information is illustrated through a bar graph. Depending on the value of the isLie parameter in the widget.xml file, the bars may be displayed vertically or horizontally.
4. To display the details using a pie chart, set the value of the graphType parameter to pie. Once done, save the changes.
EXAMPLE: When the Statistics widget is accessed in the browser, information is illustrated through a pie chart. If more than one data set is available, a dropdown list is provided to select the data set to be displayed.
5. To show the details in tabular format, set the value of the showTable parameter to T.
EXAMPLE: If the value of the showTable parameter is set to T, a table containing the statistics is displayed below the graph or chart.

Browser Settings

Before using the Statistics widget and modifying its properties:

  • Log on the CE system as an Operator user; and

  • Add the Statistics widget to the relevant tab as described in Chapter Nine > The Initial CE Landing Page with Widgets > Basic CE Widget Operations > Displaying Widgets.

Using the Statistics Widget

To use the Statistics widget:

Do the following . . .
1. Click on the relevant tab to access the Statistics widget.
2. The Statistics widget window displays the system transaction statistics or function statistics, depending on the settings defined for the widgetType parameter. NOTE: Refer to the following discussions for configuring the details to be displayed in the Statistics widget: Chapter Twenty-two: Statistics.xml File Chapter Twenty-two: jumpFunction.xml File
3. If the value of the widgetType parameter is set to jumpFunction, the data point can be clicked to proceed to the catalog of the related function.
4. The system displays the actual catalog screen. Process the relevant transaction accordingly.

Special Widget Features

  • SETTING WIDGET COLUMNS

  • DEFINING THE WIDGETS CSS FILE BY REGION OR BANK

Setting Widget Columns

When personalizing widgets, the number of columns on which the widgets are to be displayed in the CE landing page, as well as the alignment of cross column widgets, may be configured.

Initial Setting

To enable the widget column setting feature, the following settings must first be configured:

  • SQL scripts

    • Error Codes

SQL Scripts

The following SQL scripts must first be run in the database to add 2 columns in the CEUSER.SEC_WIDGET_LAYOUT table.

(Start code)

INSERT INTO CEUSER.SEC_WIDGET_ INSERT INTO CEUSER.SEC_WIDGET_LAYOUT(C_LAYOUT_ID,C_LAYOUT_NAME,C_FILE_NAME,C_DEFAULT_FLAG,C_RUN_STATUS) values (‘8AA7E5236BBB7CBA016BBB84DC610005’,‘column2’,‘layout’,‘N’,‘A’);

LAYOUT(C_LAYOUT_ID,C_LAYOUT_NAME,C_FILE_NAME,C_DEFAULT_FLAG,C_RUN_STATUS) values (‘8AA7E5236BFD69D9016BFD870B0C0010’,‘column4’,‘layout’,‘N’,‘A’);

COMMIT;

(End code)

Error Codes

Through the Error Handling function, add or modify the 000135 (the default error message for unexpected exceptions) and 000549 error codes.

The following table shows examples, which can be modified according to project requirements.

Error Key Error Code Error Message Recommended Action Error Level Variable
SYSTEM 000135 Unexpected exception. Please contact us for help. ERROR N/A
SYSTEM 000549 Please remove extra widget(s) before reducing the column. N/A WARNING N/A
  1. Add or modify the error codes 000135 and 000549 in the Error Handling function of the CE Utility.

  1. Generate the XML files for the Error Handling parameter. The generated files are stored on the following path:

    [Parameter Folder]\CE_SYS

    [Parameter Folder]\CE_SYS\ERROR\DEFAULT

Increase or Decrease the Number of Widget Columns

When personalizing widget settings, the number of columns on which widgets are to be arranged in may be defined.

Widgets may be displayed in either 2, 3, or 4 columns. To increase columns, the additional columns must be added, and the user may add or move widget instances. However, when reducing columns, the user must first move or remove extra widget instances that are included in the column to be deleted.

Column settings are applied in all widget tabs.

NOTE: In CE version 3.3.0, widgets may be displayed in 3 columns only.

Configuration

To be able to increase or decrease the number of widget columns, configurations must be made to the following CEWeb.war files.

Files to be added

  • column4.css

  • layout.jsp

column4.css

Path: [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\framework\layouts\column4

/* CEV2-04-01-17 carly.wu 20190725 S*/ /*.widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .component-container.csLayoutColumn1 { padding-left: 5px; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .layoutCol{ width: 50%; min-height: 600px; height:auto !important; }*/ .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .layoutColn4 { width: 100%; min-height: 120px; height:auto; border:1px dashed #C0C0C0; } #loading.tb.lt{ display: none; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .component-container.csLayoutCol1, .component-container.csLayoutCol3{ width: 50%; min-height: 600px; height:auto; } .oneline{ float:left; display: inline; width:99%; } .widgetMain .csLayoutContainers .component-container.csLayoutCol1{ padding-left:5px; } /* CEV2-04-01-17 carly.wu 20190725 E*/

Procedure

Do the Following …
Increase Widget Columns
1. Log on to the CE system as an operator user. In the CE landing page, click on the Personalize link.
2. In the Personalize page, the selected widgets are shown. In this example, the number of widget columns is set to 2.
3. In the Column Number field, select 3 from the dropdown list.
4. An additional column is added on the right side of the widgets area. A message is shown indicating that all changes are saved.
5. Add the relevant widgets on the newly added column (e.g., Dashboard, Quick Access, Exchange Rate) A message is shown indicating that modifications are not yet saved. Click on the Save link or the Save Changes button.
6. A confirmation message is displayed indicating that all changes are saved. Click on the Done button.
7. In the CE landing page, the widgets are arranged in 3 columns based on the personalized setting.
Decrease Widget Columns
1. Log on to the CE system as an operator user. In the CE landing page, click on the Personalize link.
2. In the Personalize page, the selected widgets are shown. In this example, the number of widget columns is set to 4.
3. In the Column Number field, select 2 from the dropdown list.
4. As the number of columns are to be reduced from 4 to 2, an error message is shown, which indicates that the widgets included in the columns to be removed must first be deleted before reducing the number of columns.
5. To remove widgets on the 2 right-most columns, click on the menu button on the upper right corner of each widget. Select the Remove option from the dropdown list. Click on the Save Changes button.
6. In the Column Number field, select 2. The widgets are then arranged into 2 columns. Save the changes and click on the Done button.
7. In the CE landing page, the widgets are arranged in 2 columns based on the personalized setting.

Left Align Cross Column Widgets

Configurations may be made to enable cross column widgets, which occupy 2 columns on the page, to always be displayed on the left side portion of the screen by default when personalizing widget settings.

NOTE: Refer to the Adjusting Widget Layouts discussion in Chapter 9 for more information on cross column widgets.

Configuration

To enable the cross column widget left alignment feature, the following settings must be configured:

  1. Modify the layout.jsp file that is located in the following path:

    [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\framework\layouts\column2

Procedure

Do the Following …
1. Log on to the CE system as an operator user. In the CE landing page, click on the Personalize link.
2. In the Personalize page, the selected widgets are shown. In this example, the number of widget columns is set to 3. The cross column widget in this example is the Inbox widget, which is automatically aligned to the left.
3. Add widget columns as required through the Column Number field. In this example, select 4 in the Column Number field to increase the column number from 3 to 4.
4. A new column is added on the right portion of the widgets area. A message is shown indicating that all changes are saved. The cross column widget remains aligned to the left.
5. Add the relevant widgets on the newly added column. A message is shown indicating that modifications are not yet saved. Click on the Save link or the Save Changes button.
6. A confirmation message is displayed indicating that all changes are saved. Click on the Done button.
7. In the CE landing page, the widgets are arranged in 4 columns based on the personalized setting. To decrease widget column numbers, click on the Personalize link.
8. To reduce the column number, the widgets set in the column to be deleted must first be removed or moved to a different column. Remove the relevant widgets and then reduce the column from 4 to 3 through the Column Number field.
NOTE: If the column number is reduced while widgets are still existing in the column to be removed, an error message is shown.
9. A confirmation message is shown once all the changes made are saved. Click on the Done button.
10. In the CE landing page, the widgets are arranged in 3 columns based on the personalized setting.

Right Align Cross Column Widgets

Configurations may be made to enable cross column widgets, which occupy 2 columns on the page, to always be displayed on the right side portion of the screen by default when personalizing widget settings.

NOTE:

i. Refer to the Adjusting Widget Layouts discussion in Chapter 9 for more information on Cross Column Widgets.

ii. The right align cross column widgets feature is only applied for 3 or 4-column widget settings.

Configuration

To enable the right aligned cross widget column feature, the following configuration must be made:

For 3 Widget Columns

Refer to the Adjusting Widget Layouts > Layout.jsp file discussion for the updates to be made on the layout.jsp file for 3 widget column setting.

For 4 Widget Columns

Create a backup copy of the layout.jsp file located in the following path:

[CEWeb.war folder]\widgets\framework\layouts\column4

Create a new file with the same name (i.e., layout.jsp) in this same path with the following content:
