Procedure

Example
1. Log on to the CE system as an operator user. In the CE landing page, click on the Personalize link.
2. In the Personalize page, the selected widgets are shown. In this example, the number of widget columns is set to 2.
3. Add widget columns as required through the Column Number field. In this example, select 4 in the Column Number field to increase the number of widget columns from 2 to 4.
4. The new columns are added on the right side of the widgets area. A message is shown indicating that all changes are saved. The cross column widget is automatically aligned to the right.
5. Add the relevant widgets on the newly added columns. A message is shown indicating that modifications are not yet saved. Click on the Save link or the Save Changes button.
6. A confirmation message is displayed indicating that all changes are saved. Click on the Done button.
7. In the CE landing page, the widgets are arranged in 4 columns based on the personalized setting. To decrease columns, click on the Personalize link.
8. To reduce the column number, the widgets set in the column to be deleted must first be removed or moved to a different column.
NOTE: If the column number is reduced while widgets are still existing in the column/s to be removed, an error message is shown.
Remove the relevant widgets and then reduce the column from 4 to 2 through the Column Number field.
9. A confirmation message is shown once all the changes made are saved. Click on the Done button.
10. In the CE landing page, the widgets are arranged in 2 columns based on the personalized setting.

Defining the Widgets CSS File By Region or Bank

Different CSS file on widgets may be used for each regional country code or bank. Different entities may have different CSS style for each widget instance and different CSS style for widget framework.

NOTE:

  1. In transactions, only the regional value of the logged on unit is used.

  2. Even if the logged on has child companies in different regions, the regional value of the logged on group is still the one used.

  3. This feature does not support 4 widget column setting.

Configuration

The widgetStyleByEntity.xml file is used to define the widget instances that are to use different CSS styles either by region or by bank. This file is also used to indicate the CSS style for the widget framework. This file is stored on the following path:

[Parameter Folder]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\framework

The system applies different CSS styles for widgets defined in this xml file while applying one common CSS styles to widget instances that are not indicated in this file. If this file does not exist, the system follows the standard logic of using one common CSS style for widgets.

NOTE: This xml file is maintained manually, and is not generated by the CE Utility.

widgetStyleByEntity.xml File Sample Content:

<?xml version="1.0” encoding="utf-8”?> <config> <widgets BYBANK="Y” BYREGION="Y”> <widget BYBANK="Y” BYREGION="N”>MainMenu</widget> <widget BYBANK="Y” BYREGION="N”>Dashboard</widget> </widgets> <framework BYBANK="Y” BYREGION="Y”> </framework> </config>

The widgetStyleByEntity.xml file may be configured using the following details:

Node Name Description Attribute
widgets - Configure ‘by bank/region’ options for widget instances widgets@BYBANK This attribute is a global setting for all widget instances. Y: Use different CSS styles by bank (different {BANK} folder) N: Use a common CSS style for all banks. It is the default value.
widgets@BYREGION This attribute is a global setting for all widget instances. Y: Use different CSS styles by region (different {REGION} folder) N: Use a common CSS style for all regions. It is the default value.
widgets > widget This attribute is a special setting for the specified widget instance. These settings are applied prior to the global setting. Specify the widget instance name.
widgets > widget@BYBANK This attribute is a special setting applied for the specified widget instance. Y: Use different CSS styles by bank (different {BANK} folder) N: Use a common CSS style for all banks. It is the default value.
widgets > widget@BYREGION This attribute is a special setting applied for the specified widget instance. Y: Use different CSS styles by region (different {REGION} folder) N: Use a common CSS style for all regions. It is the default value.
framework - Configure ‘by bank/region’ options for widget framework framework@BYBANK This attribute is used to control the widget framework. Y: Use different templates by bank (different {BANK} folder) N: Use a common template for all banks. It is the default value.
framework@BYREGION This attribute is used to control the widget framework. Y: Use different templates by region (different {REGION} folder) N: Use a common template for all regions. It is the default value.

Procedure

Do the Following …
All widget instances use different CSS styles for different regions
1. In this sample procedure, the dashboard widget and main menu widgets are used as examples to show that different CSS styles are used for all widgets per region. 2 regions are used: CN and US. Create the relevant folders to store widget CSS files for both regions. NOTE: The widget CSS file used for different regions must have the same file name. Examples: Dashboard Widget and Main Menu Widget Dashboard Widget Folders Default Dashboard.css file for global office Dashboard.css file for CN region Dashboard.css file for US region
Main Menu Widget Folders Default MainMenu.css file for global office MainMenu.css file for CN region MainMenu.css file for US region
NOTE: Image files indicated in the relevant CSS file must also be stored on the same region folder. Example, in the dashboard.css file for the CN region, the URL value is note_bg.png. Thus, the note_bg.png file must be stored on the same CN region folder on which the dashboard.css file is located (e.g., [CEWeb.war folder]\widgets\Dashboard\Bank]\CN\note_bg.png) Example
Otherwise, these image files may be stored in the main widget folder and the corresponding URL indicated in the css file must be modified. Example
2. In the widgetStyleByEntity.xml file, the widgets and framework nodes must be set to BYREGION=”Y”
3. Log on the CE system as an operator which regional code is set to CN for the relevant bank (e.g., ENBDAEOP1). The Dashboard and Main Menu widgets are displayed according to the css files stored in the CN region folder. E.g.: [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\MainMenu\[Bank]\CN\mainmenu.css [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\Dashboard\CN\dashboard.css
4. Log on the CE system as an operator which regional code is set to US for the relevant bank (e.g., USOP02). The Dashboard and Main Menu widgets are displayed according to the css files stored in the US region folder. E.g.: [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\MainMenu\[Bank]\US\mainmenu.css [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\Dashboard\US\dashboard.css
5. Log on the CE system as a global user. The Dashboard and Main Menu widgets are displayed according to the css files stored in the main Dashboard and Main Menu widget folders. E.g.: [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\MainMenu\mainmenu.css [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\Dashboard\dashboard.css
Some widgets use different CSS style for different regions while some widget instances use a common css style
1. In this sample procedure, all widget instances use a different css style for each region except for the main menu widget. The dashboard widget is used in this example to represent all the other widgets. 2 regions are used: CN and US. Create the relevant folders to store CSS files to be used globally and for each region. NOTE: The CSS file used for different regions must have the same file name. Examples: Dashboard Widget and Main Menu Widget Dashboard Widget Folders Default Dashboard.css file for global office Dashboard.css file for CN region Dashboard.css file for US region
Main Menu Widget Folder Default MainMenu.css file for global office
2. In the widgetStyleByEntity.xml file, the widgets and framework nodes must be set to: For all widgets BYREGION=”Y” For the MainMenu widget BYREGION=”N”
3. Log on the CE system as an operator which regional code is set to CN (e.g., CHINAOP1). The main menu widget uses the global css style, while the dashboard widget uses the regional style based on the css file stored in the CN region folder (e.g.[CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\Dashboard\CN\dashboard.css).
4. Log on the CE system as an operator which regional code is set to US (e.g., USOP1). The main menu widget uses the global css style, while the dashboard widget uses the regional style based on the css file stored in the US region folder (e.g.[CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\Dashboard\US\dashboard.css).
5. Log on the CE system as a global user. The Dashboard and Main Menu widgets are displayed according to the css files stored in the main Dashboard and Main Menu widget folders. E.g.: [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\MainMenu\mainmenu.css [CEWeb.war Folder]\widgets\Dashboard\dashboard.css
The widget framework use different CSS styles for different regions
1. In this sample procedure, 2 regions are used: CN and US. The default global framework.xml file is stored on the following path: [Parameter Fodler]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\framework Since the CSS file for modes and wrappers are defined in the default global framework.xml file, the regional folders must be created under the framework folder in this main global path. E.g. [Parameter Fodler]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\framework\[Bank]\CN [Parameter Fodler]\CE_SYS\WIDGETS\framework\[Bank] \US NOTE: The CSS file used for different regions must have the same file name. Widget Framework Folders Default framework.xml file for global office framework.xml file for CN region framework.xml file for US region
2. The global modes and wrapper folders are located in this path: [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets Create the regional folders for modes and wrappers under the default global modes and wrapper folders. E.g.: Modes [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\modes\[Bank]\CN\config.css [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\modes\[Bank]\US\config.css Wrappers [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\wrappers\[Bank]\CN\wrapper.css [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\wrappers\[Bank]\US\wrapper.css NOTE: The CSS file used for different regions must have the same file name. Global Folders Modes Wrappers CN Region Folders Modes Wrappers US Region Folders Modes Wrappers
3. The column 2 and column 3 layout folders are located in this path: [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\framework\layouts Create the regional folders for column 2 and column 3 layout under the default column layout folders. E.g.: Column 2 [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\framework\layouts\column2\[Bank]\CN\column2.css [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\framework\layouts\column2\[Bank]\US\column2.css Column 3 [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\framework\layouts\column2\[Bank]\CN\column3.css [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\framework\layouts\column2\[Bank]\US\column3.css NOTE: The CSS file used for different regions must have the same file name. Global Column 2 and Column 3 Folders Column 2 Folder CN Region US Region Column 3 Folder CN Region US Region
4. Log on to the CE system as an operator user which regional code is CN (e.g., CHINAOP1). The displayed widget CSS style is based on the CSS files for the CN region. [CEWeb.war folder]\widgets\framework\layouts\column3\[Bank]\CN\column3.css [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\modes\[Bank]\CN\config.css [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\wrappers\[Bank]\CN\wrapper.css
5. Log on to the CE system as an operator user which regional code is US (e.g., USOP1). The displayed widget CSS style is based on the CSS files for the US region. [CEWeb.war folder]\widgets\framework\layouts\column3\[Bank]\US\column3.css [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\modes\[Bank]\US\config.css [CEWeb.war folder]\theme\default\widgets\wrappers\[Bank]\US\wrapper.css
6. Log on to the CE system as a global user. The displayed widget CSS style is based on the global CSS files.

Glossary

Glossary

a

Administrator The type of CE Utility user with rights to create Administrator and Operator users and define transaction function parameters such as GAPI rules, SWIFT settings, and accounting rules.
** **
Application Server Server where the CE system is actually deployed and where CE processes the business logic and parameter operations.
Attribute Pertains to a Business component. Its specific settings regulate the behavior of functions in processing transactions. Unlike the main program (Control component), which provides the general purpose of the function, attributes define the actual actions to be performed by the function. A function may use several attributes; this group of one or more attributes is called an Attribute rule.
** **
Authorization Rule A group of settings that determine when a transaction is considered authorized.

B

Bankbanner.lbi An LBI file that is modified to change the layout of the CE system header.

C

Calculator widget A widget is a tool for basic calculation operations.
Calendar A CE functionality used for selecting a specific date.
Calendar Events Widget A widget tool that shows basic calendar details, weekends and holidays, notes on specific dates and marked dates.
Catalog A set of criteria that is used for filtering the records to be retrieved into, and subsequently processed in, a transaction function.
Catalog Screens A CE in a transaction function used by the end-user of the system for selecting the relevant record to process in the transaction function.
CE Utility Short for Customer Enterprise Utility Workbench. This is the main tool for building parameters in CE.
CEMETA The database user profile that is assigned access and usage rights to the CEMETA tablespace.
CETAGS System or predefined tags in CE that are used to identify and attach certain attributes to the JSP transaction screen. These allow the JSP file to retrieve information from the Standing Data module and to generate option field values for Select-type or Interpreter fields as defined in the Field Conversion function of the CE Utility.
CEWeb.war The folder that contains the business parameter files which are in the original format as JS or JSP.
Change User Profile A CE function used for changing the password and e-mail address of the logged-on user.
Clause Descriptions, details, narratives, or message contents that are commonly or frequently used in the transactions. These clauses may be predefined in the system to avoid the manual input of long phrases at runtime processing.
Clause Page The CE transaction function popup window that allows the end-user of the system to select predefined clauses as input for the transaction.
Client The CE system’s user browser interface.
Confirmation Page A page that is displayed if the change password or change e-mail process is successful.
Criteria Search widget A widget tool used for defining filter settings to search for specific records.
CUBK Data that are inquired or retrieved in a transaction process, usually Customer or Bank data.
Customer Enterprise (CE) The Eximbills business-to-business (B2B) solution that provides bank customers with a convenient and secure single window for processing and inquiring on all their trade finance, open account, and payments transactions.
Customer Enterprise Utility Workbench See CE Utility.

D

DAP Stands for Data Access Permission. This refers to a user’s rights to access specific data or records.
Database An application used for the management, storage, and retrieval of data.
Data Source A source of digitized data (e.g., database, connection to a database).
Dashboard widget A widget tool used to access a specific catalog and subsequently view or process a record.

E

End-user The actual user running the CE business functions.
Event A grouping of activities that occur in the life cycle of a specific type of transaction.
Event JS file A JS file that contains the function level calculation functions that serve as event handlers of the functions defined in the Function JS file.
Event List Page A CE transaction page that shows a list of the transaction’s events.
Event Page A CE transaction page that displays the data of a transaction at a particular stage in the processing flow.
Exchange Rate widget A widget tool used for determining and calculating the current exchange rates of currencies.
Eximbills The flagship product of China Systems, which provides support for advanced e-commerce, open account, and trade-related services.

F

FAP Stands for Function Access Permission. This refers to a user’s rights to perform specific function operations.
Field The smallest unit that can hold data.
Footer The lowest section of the CE page which displays the copyright information of the CE system, as well as links that point to information about China Systems.
Freemarker Template A template that can be embedded into the JSP file.
FTL See Freemarker Template*.*
Function Also referred to as transaction function. This is the actual CE browser-side function that is run by an end-user to perform a specific operation or process for a business transaction.
Function Group A grouping of CE browser-side functions that is organized based on the common usage and purpose of the functions. A function group is set up in the CE Utility.
Function JS file A JS file that contains the function level methods, calculations and validations that control the behavior of specific fields in a transaction page.
Function Tool Pertains to clause, lookup button (Inquire CUBK), transaction template, and calendar

G

GAPI Stands for Generic Application Programming Interface; it is a component that facilitates the integration of the CE system with the processes of other systems, such that the CE system is able to communicate with other systems for data exchange, data transfer, and data inquiry.
GetMenuArray A CETAG used for generating the function tree menu content.

H

Header The uppermost section of a page.
Home Tab The default tab provided on first accessing the CE browser. It contains two widgets: Main Menu and Welcome.
HTML Stands for Hyper Text Markup Language; the main markup language for web pages, HTML elements are the basic building-blocks of web pages. It consists of tags enclosed in angle brackets within the web page content, and has start tags (opening tags) and end tags (closing tags). In between these tags are text, tags, comments and other types of text-based content.

I

IBM WebSphere Application Server The application server service by IBM Websphere that facilitates the operation and maintenance of the application processes of systems such as CE.
Inbox A facility for accessing and processing transactions in three ways: by product; by transaction status; and by product and transaction status.
IncludeFile An EXIMTAG used for attaching a file to the JSP.
Inquire CUBK A CE transaction function popup window that allows the end-user to select a record which details populate transaction fields as input.
Inquire History The CE transaction functions that are used for inquiring on the history of a transaction; specifically, the events of a transaction.

J

JavaScript A scripting language that can interact with HTML source codes and has dynamic content.
JS File A file containing JavaScript codes or commands for creating the look and feel of the system. The MainMenu.js and other JS files are located in the JS folder under the Web Server Drive.
JSP Stands for JavaServer Pages. This technology enables the creation of dynamic web content and development of web-based applications that are server- and platform- independent. Transaction screens, which are the actual web pages displayed when running a function in the CE browser, are saved as JSP files.
JSP Template A page template that defines the sections that are common to all transaction screens: page header, main menu, and page footer.

L

Landing Page Tthe page that is displayed to the end-user upon successfully logging on the system.
Logon Page The page which users access in order to log in to CE.
Look and Feel Pertains to the CE user interface that is designed when the different elements that make up a functional transaction page are put together based on a desired output
L&F See Look and Feel*.*

M

Main Menu widget A CE widget that provides the list of CE products and the corresponding functions.
Module Pertains to a bank’s product or service.

N

Notice widget A widget used for viewing the notification messages sent to the current (logged-on) user.

O

Operator The type of CE Utility user with parameter and transaction module configuration rights.
Operator Class See User Class.

P

Parameter Any user-controlled configuration that defines a factor or logic within a set of interrelated operations; performs a specific action in a group of processes; or produces a categorical result or setting.
Parameter Drive The location of the CE parameter files, one of the two main folders of an CE environment. Its path is defined in the GEN_XML_ROOTPATH system parameter.
Protocol Manager Function The CE Utility function that is used to configure, manage, and maintain the communication protocols used by CE for connecting with other systems.
Product Catalog A product catalog is used for setting the catalog criteria for the events pertaining to a business transaction master record.

Q

Quick Access Widget A widget used to quickly access frequently used functions.

R

Recent Functions widget A widget used for directly accessing the functions that have been recently run by the logged-on user.
Record Pertains to the business transaction.
RTL Security Parameter This security parameter is used to change how widgets, transaction functions, and error messages are displayed on the CE page: certain elements are re-arranged from right to left.

S

Schema The structure and layout of objects within the database. In Oracle, a schema is associated with a specific database user and is comprised of database objects such as tables and views.
Screen A function’s transaction screen. This is the actual webpage displayed when running a function in the CE browser.
Security Module A group of CE security and system maintenance functions. With these functions, the required security and system settings are initially configured to enable a CE user to run any security or business function from the CE system.
SQL Stands for Structured Query Language. This is a standard interactive and programming language for retrieving and updating data in the database.
SQL Statements The building blocks of SQL software and programming. An SQL statement definition leads to specific output and always begins with a command (e.g., Create, Select, Insert).
Standard.css A CSS file that is modified for system purposes such as changing the elements of objects in the screen like border, object position, color and size of text.
Standing Data Pertains to customer account numbers, bank details, customer details and exchange rates.
Statistics Widget A widget used for viewing a graphic representation of transaction statistics in the whole CE system, or in specific functions.
Summary widget A widget used for viewing the summary details of transactions through a specific type of catalog: inbox catalog, function catalog, or product catalog.
Super Administrator The type of CE Utility user with rights to administrative tasks such as configuring business units; defining data sources; and creating Super Administrator and Administrator user profiles.
SYS_screens.xml An XML file where all CE JSP files are defined in.
System CSS Classes Used in CE for field validation and date formatting
System Methods Predefined methods that are available for use in any level of calculation.
System Parameters The references or values that are defined to control the behavior of CE during transaction processing on the browser and in the CE Utility.

T

TemplateContent A CETAG used for including the transaction JSP files into the JSP template.
TransRelease.jsp The JSP template for the Authorise or Release screen
Transaction Function The CE Utility function group that consists of functions used for defining the actual business parameters of transaction functions. See Function also.
Transaction Screen See Screen.
Transaction Template A CE transaction function popup window that allows the end-user of the system to save and load transaction templates.

U

Upload Message widget A function is used for directly uploading a file without having to go through the relevant function with upload functionality.
User Class A user’s specific authorization right or level.

W

Web Server The server that receives data from the client (i.e., JSP and JS information), converts it to XML format, passes it to the application server for processing, and passes the processed info from the application server to the client.
Web Service Setting A transaction function used to generate the WebService.xml file.
Welcome widget A widget that displays the welcome message, the name of the logged user, the current and last successful login time.
Widget A small application that can be installed and run within a web page by an end-user.
WIDGET_ACTION_POPUP A security parameter that is used to control whether the system pops up a new window when a widget hyperlink or button is clicked.
Widget Maintain A function used to create and maintain widgets used in the CE browser.

X

XML Stands for Extensible Markup Language. This is the format used by CE for the communication between the client (browser) and the server.
XML Generator Function The CE Utility function that is used to generate the corresponding XML files for a specific parameter setting.
